The Judge's Prohibition from Hindering Creditors
Ruling with proof from hadith about not hindering creditors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge intervening between a debtor and creditors after release, and identify the hadith proof used.

Core Idea
A judge must not block creditors from pursuing debtors after release.

This passage from a Hanafi legal text addresses a practical scenario: a debtor is imprisoned but later released because no wealth is found. What is the judge's role after release? The text rules that the judge must not stand between the debtor and his creditors; instead, creditors retain the right to demand payment. A hadith from the Prophet (ﷺ) supports this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge intervening between a released debtor and his creditors. The ruling is that such intervention is prohibited (haram).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith narrated by Hirmas ibn Habib from his father from his grandfather: 'I came to the Prophet with a creditor of mine, and he said to me, 'Keep hold of him,' then said, 'O brother of Bani Tamim, what do you intend to do with your prisoner?'
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command 'Keep hold of him' indicates that the creditor is allowed to personally pursue the debtor. By implication, the judge should not prevent this.
The wajh is that the Prophet did not order the judge to intervene.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage does not mention any intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab disagreement. It presents a unanimous ruling (muttafaq alayh).
5
Apply the ruling to practice
The judge's role ends with releasing the debtor; he must not give any order that hinders the creditor from demanding his right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۰۸ (۲۱) ولا يحول بينه وبين غرمائه

[۱۲۹۰۸ (۲۱) اور حائل نہ ہو اس کے اور اس کے قرض خواہوں کے درمیان۔
مقروض کو قید سے تو نکال دے گا لیکن قرض خواہ کو کہا جائے گا کہ مقروض کے پیچھے لگار ہے۔ جب اس کے پاس رقم آئے قرض خواہ اس سے اپنا حق وصول کر لے۔ قاضی مقروض اور قرض خواہ کے درمیان حائل نہ ہو۔
حدیث میں ہے۔ اخبرنا هرماس بن حبيب عن ابيه عن جده قال: اتيت النبي الله بغريم لي فقال لي الزمه ثم قال لی یا اخا بنی تمیم ماتريد ان تفعل با سیرک؟ (ب) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الدین هل تحبس، ج ۲، ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۳۶۲۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مقروض کے پیچھے قرضخواہ کو لگنے کی اجازت دے۔
غرماء : غریم کی جمع ہے قرض خواہ۔ یحول : حائل ہونا۔
He should not intervene between him and his creditors. And it is not allowed for the judge to come between the debtor and his creditors. The judge will release him from imprisonment but will tell the creditor to stick to the debtor; when he gets money, the creditor can collect his right. The judge should not intervene. A hadith: Hirmas ibn Habib narrated from his father from his grandfather: I came to the Prophet (ﷺ) with a creditor of mine, and he said to me, 'Keep hold of him,' then said, 'O brother of Bani Tamim, what do you intend to do with your prisoner?' This hadith indicates that the creditor should be allowed to chase the debtor. 'Ghurama' is plural of 'gharim' meaning creditor. 'Yahulu' means to intervene.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: after a debtor is released from imprisonment (because his wealth could not be found), the judge should not stand between the debtor and his creditors. Instead, the judge should inform the creditor to continue demanding his right. The proof is the hadith in which the Prophet (ﷺ) told a creditor to keep hold of his debtor. The passage also defines key terms: ghurama (creditors) and yahulu (to intervene).

Key Terms
غرماء (ghurama): plural of gharim, meaning creditors
یحول (yahulu): means to intervene or come between

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a judge intervening between a debtor and his creditors after releasing the debtor from imprisonment?
A) It is obligatory for the judge to intervene.
B) The judge is prohibited from intervening.
C) The judge must imprison the debtor again.
D) The judge should take the debt from the debtor's family.

Key Takeaway
A judge must not obstruct creditors from pursuing a released debtor; the debt remains enforceable.

Parent Not Imprisoned for Child's Debt Except for Maintenance
Ruling with proof on parental imprisonment for child's debts and maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on imprisonment of a parent for a child's debt and explain the exception for maintenance refusal, citing the supporting proofs.

Core Idea
A parent is not imprisoned for a child's debt, but may be imprisoned for refusing maintenance when the child is at risk.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on whether a parent can be imprisoned for financial obligations related to their child. The default ruling is that a parent cannot be imprisoned for the child's debts because the Hanafi view considers the child's wealth to belong to the parent. However, an important exception exists for maintenance (nafaqah) refusal, where imprisonment becomes a tool to compel provision. We will explore the evidences from hadith and Quran that underpin this distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Identify the default rule: a parent (father, grandfather, maternal grandfather) is not to be imprisoned for the debt of his child (son, daughter, or grandchildren).
2
Identify the exception
Recognize that the rule changes if the parent refuses to provide maintenance (nafaqah) to the child when the child's life is endangered.
The exception is triggered by refusal to pay nafaqah, not by any other debt.
3
Examine the proof for the general ruling
Analyze the hadith: 'You and your wealth belong to your father' (Ibn Majah). This indicates that a child's wealth is considered the father's property, so any 'debt' from the parent to the child is not a true debt but a gift or favor.
Thubut: zanni; Dalala: zanni
4
Examine the proof for the exception
Study the Quranic verses (2:233, 65:6) that establish the obligation of maintenance. When the parent refuses to provide essential maintenance, imprisonment becomes a permissible means to enforce this obligation.
The verses use imperative forms indicating obligation (wujub).
5
Explain the legal reasoning
Understand why the two scenarios differ: In debt, the parent is essentially taking back what is already theirs, so no actual debt exists. In maintenance, the parent is neglecting a fresh obligation, and imprisonment is used to prevent harm to the child.
The maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applies: the intent behind imprisonment changes the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۱۰] (۲۳) ولا يُحبس الوالد في دين ولده الا اذا امتنع من الانفاق عليه
اور والد قید نہیں کئے جائیں گے اپنی اولاد کے دین میں ، مگر جبکہ رک جائے اس پر خرچ کرنے سے۔
والد پر بیٹے ، بیٹی ، پوتے پوتی، نواسے نواسی کا قرض ہو تو اس کی وجہ سے والد یا دادا یا نا نا قد نہیں کئے جائیں گے۔

ان لوگوں کا مال والد کا مال ہے۔ پہلے گزر چکا ہے۔ عن عمرو بن شعیب عن ابيه عن جده قال: جاء رجل الى النبي الله فقال ان ابی اجتاج مالی فقال انت و مالک لابیک وقال رسول الله الله الله ان اولادكم من اطيب كسبكم فكلوا من اموالکم (الف) (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ماللرجل من مال ولده ، ص ۳۲۸، نمبر ۲۲۹۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اولاد کا مال باپ کا ہے اس لئے ان لوگوں کا جو قرض باپ یا دادا پر ہے وہ قرض کے بجائے احسان ہے۔ اس لئے ان قرضوں کی وجہ سے قید نہیں کئے جائیں گے (۲) آیت میں ہے کہ ان کے ساتھ احسان کا معاملہ کرو اور قید کرنا احسان اور احترام کے خلاف ہے اس لئے بھی قید نہیں کئے جائیں گے۔ آیت یہ ہے۔ وصاحبهما في الدنيا معروفا (آیت ۱۵ سورۃ لقمان (۳۱) اس آیت میں ہے کہ ان لوگوں کے ساتھ احترام کا معاملہ کرو۔ لیکن اگر اولا د کو کھانے کا خرچ نہ دے اور اولاد کی ہلاکت کا خطرہ ہو تو والد قید کئے جائیں گے تا کہ نفقہ دے اور اولا د ہلاک نہ ہوں (۲) آیت میں ہے کہ اولا دکا نفقہ واجب ہے۔ وعلى المولود له رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف (ب) (آیت ۲۳۳ ، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) دوسری آیت میں ہے۔ فان ارضعن لكم فأتوهن أجورهن وأتمروا بينكم بمعروف (آيت ، سورۃ الطلاق ۶۵) ان آیتوں سے معلوم ہوا کہ باپ پر اولاد کا نفقہ واجب ہے اس لئے نفقہ دینے میں کوتاہی کرے تو قید کیا جا سکتا ہے
And the parent is not imprisoned for the debt of his child, unless he refrains from spending on him. And a parent will not be imprisoned for the debt of his child, unless he stops spending on him. The debt of a son, daughter, grandson, granddaughter, grandson through daughter, granddaughter through daughter upon the father, grandfather, or maternal grandfather will not cause imprisonment. Their wealth is the father's wealth, as has passed. [Hadith] from 'Amr ibn Shu'aib from his father from his grandfather: A man came to the Prophet (ﷺ) and said, 'My father is in need of my wealth.' He said, 'You and your wealth belong to your father.' And the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said, 'Indeed your children are among the best of your earnings, so eat from your wealth.' This hadith indicates that the child's wealth belongs to the father, so the debt of these people upon the father or grandfather is a favor, not a debt. Therefore, they will not be imprisoned for such debts. And the verse says, 'Accompany them in the world with kindness' (31:15). This indicates to treat them with honor, and imprisonment contradicts honor. So they are not imprisoned. However, if he does not give the children food and there is fear of their destruction, then the parent will be imprisoned so that he provides maintenance and the children are not destroyed. The verse says, 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing appropriately' (2:233). And another verse, 'So if they suckle for you, then give them their due recompense and consult among yourselves in a reasonable manner' (65:6). These verses indicate that the father is obligated to provide maintenance for the children, so if he is negligent in providing maintenance, he can be imprisoned.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage addresses the imprisonment of a parent for the debt of his child. The general ruling is that a parent is not imprisoned for such a debt because the child's wealth is considered the parent's in the Hanafi view, based on the hadith 'You and your wealth belong to your father.' Therefore, these are not true debts but rather obligations of favor. However, there is an exception: if the parent refuses to provide maintenance (nafaqah) for the child, to the point that the child's life is at risk, then the parent can be imprisoned to enforce the duty of maintenance. The proof is from the Qur'anic verses on maintenance. The passage thus distinguishes between debts (which do not lead to imprisonment of parents) and maintenance obligations (which do, in extreme cases).

Key Terms
والد (walid): father or grandfather
نفقہ (nafaqah): maintenance for children

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, a father can be imprisoned for which of the following?
A) For any debt he owes to his child.
B) For refusing to pay a debt to a third party that the child guaranteed.
C) For refusing to provide food and clothing to his minor child, endangering the child's life.
D) For not paying maintenance to his ex-wife.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a parent is immune from imprisonment for a child's debt because the child's wealth is considered the parent's, but imprisonment is a valid tool to enforce maintenance when the child's life is at risk.

Woman as Judge: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on the permissibility of a woman serving as a judge except in hudud and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women serving as judges and identify the exceptions.

Core Idea
A woman may judge all cases except hudud and qisas.

This lesson presents the Hanafi position that a woman is qualified to serve as a judge in most matters. The ruling is based on general permissibility, with two important exceptions rooted in evidentiary rules.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its general ruling
Identify the act (woman acting as judge) and the default ruling (permissible).
Default permissibility (ibahah asliyyah) unless evidence restricts.
2
Identify the two exceptions
List hudud and qisas as cases where a woman cannot judge.
Hudud: fixed punishments; qisas: retaliation.
3
Understand the link between judgment and testimony
A judge relies on witnesses; women's testimony is not accepted in hudud and qisas, so she cannot decide those cases.
Evidentiary limitation drives the ruling.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school prohibits women from judging altogether, unlike the Hanafi position.
This difference arises from different usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۱۱] (۲۴) ويجوز قضاء المرأة في كل شيء الا في الحدود والقصاص
اور جائز ہے عورت کو قاضی ہوتا ہر معاملے میں سوائے حدود اور قصاص کے۔ عورت ہر چیز کی قاضی بن سکتی ہے البتہ حدود اور قصاص کا قاضی نہیں بن سکتی۔ حدود اور قصاص میں عورت کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے تو اس کا فیصلہ کیا کرے گی (۲) حدیث مرسل میں ہے۔ عن الزهری قال: مضت السنة من رسول الله الا الله والخليفتين من بعده الا تجوز شهادة النساء في الحدود (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۰۹افی شهادة النساء في الحدود، ج خامس، ص ۵۲۸، ۲۸۷۰۵ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب هل تجوز شهادة النساء مع الرجال في الحدود وغيره، ج ثامن، ص ۱۳۳۰ نمبر ۵۴۱۲ ارسن سیمی ، باب شهادة في الطلاق والرجعة ومافي معناهما من النكاح والقصاص والحدود، ج عاشر ص ۲۵۰، نمبر ۲۰۵۲۸) اس میں ہے کہ حدود اور قصاص میں عورت کی گواہی مقبول نہیں تو اس معاملے کا قاضی بننا کیسے درست ہو گا ؟ اس لئے کہ قاضی تو گواہوں کی گواہی لیکر فیصلہ کرتا ہے۔
And the judgment of a woman is permissible in everything except hudud and qisas. And it is permissible for a woman to be a judge in every matter except hudud and qisas. A woman can be a judge in everything, but she cannot be a judge in hudud and qisas. This is because in hudud and qisas, a woman's testimony is not accepted, so how will she decide? [There is] a mursal hadith from al-Zuhri: The sunnah from the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) and the two caliphs after him is that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud. This hadith indicates that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud and qisas, so how can she be a judge in these matters? Because a judge decides based on witnesses.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage states that a woman is qualified to serve as a judge in all types of cases except those involving hudud (fixed penalties for crimes like theft, zina) and qisas (retaliation for murder or injury). The reason given is that in hudud and qisas, female testimony is not accepted (as established by a mursal hadith), and a judge relies on witnesses. Therefore, she cannot act as a judge where she cannot hear valid testimony. This ruling reflects the Hanafi position that women are generally eligible for the judiciary except in these specific areas.

Key Terms
حدود (hudud): fixed punishments for crimes against God (e.g., theft, zina, drinking)
قصاص (qisas): retaliation for bodily harm; equitable punishment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, in which cases is a woman not allowed to serve as a judge?
A) In divorce cases.
B) In hudud and qisas.
C) In financial disputes.
D) In all criminal matters.

Key Takeaway
A woman is qualified as a judge in all cases except hudud and qisas due to evidentiary limitations.

The Proof and the Dispute: Women’s Testimony and Judging Hudud/Qisas
Proof and dispute on women as judges

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the hadith evidence and compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on female judges.

Core Idea
The exclusion of hudud and qisas is based on a mursal hadith that women's testimony is not accepted in these cases.

This lesson focuses on the evidentiary basis for the exception and the ensuing cross-madhhab debate. The Hanafi school applies the rule narrowly, while the Shafi'i school generalizes it to prohibit women from all judicial roles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dalil (mursal hadith)
Locate the hadith from al-Zuhri and note that it is mursal (zanni al-thubut).
The hadith states that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud.
2
Analyze its thubut and dalala
Determine that both transmission and indication are zanni (speculative).
Mursal hadiths are generally considered weak by some, but Hanafis accept them under certain conditions.
3
Trace the logical link
Understand the reasoning: a judge decides based on witnesses -> if women's testimony is not accepted, she cannot judge those cases.
This is a form of qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Understand Shafi'i counter-proof
Shafi'i rely on Quranic verses (2:282, 4:34) to argue women lack full legal capacity for authoritative positions.
They see the testimony limitation as evidence of a general deficiency.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Hanafis argue that those verses are specific to testimony and guardianship, not judiciary; the mursal hadith is limited to hudud, so general permissibility remains.
The Hanafi position is considered mufta bihi within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۱۱] (۲۴) ويجوز قضاء المرأة في كل شيء الا في الحدود والقصاص
اور جائز ہے عورت کو قاضی ہوتا ہر معاملے میں سوائے حدود اور قصاص کے۔ عورت ہر چیز کی قاضی بن سکتی ہے البتہ حدود اور قصاص کا قاضی نہیں بن سکتی۔ حدود اور قصاص میں عورت کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے تو اس کا فیصلہ کیا کرے گی (۲) حدیث مرسل میں ہے۔ عن الزهری قال: مضت السنة من رسول الله الا الله والخليفتين من بعده الا تجوز شهادة النساء في الحدود (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۰۹افی شهادة النساء في الحدود، ج خامس، ص ۵۲۸، ۲۸۷۰۵ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب هل تجوز شهادة النساء مع الرجال في الحدود وغيره، ج ثامن، ص ۱۳۳۰ نمبر ۵۴۱۲ ارسن سیمی ، باب شهادة في الطلاق والرجعة ومافي معناهما من النكاح والقصاص والحدود، ج عاشر ص ۲۵۰، نمبر ۲۰۵۲۸) اس میں ہے کہ حدود اور قصاص میں عورت کی گواہی مقبول نہیں تو اس معاملے کا قاضی بننا کیسے درست ہو گا ؟ اس لئے کہ قاضی تو گواہوں کی گواہی لیکر فیصلہ کرتا ہے۔
And the judgment of a woman is permissible in everything except hudud and qisas. And it is permissible for a woman to be a judge in every matter except hudud and qisas. A woman can be a judge in everything, but she cannot be a judge in hudud and qisas. This is because in hudud and qisas, a woman's testimony is not accepted, so how will she decide? [There is] a mursal hadith from al-Zuhri: The sunnah from the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) and the two caliphs after him is that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud. This hadith indicates that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud and qisas, so how can she be a judge in these matters? Because a judge decides based on witnesses.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage states that a woman is qualified to serve as a judge in all types of cases except those involving hudud (fixed penalties for crimes like theft, zina) and qisas (retaliation for murder or injury). The reason given is that in hudud and qisas, female testimony is not accepted (as established by a mursal hadith), and a judge relies on witnesses. Therefore, she cannot act as a judge where she cannot hear valid testimony. This ruling reflects the Hanafi position that women are generally eligible for the judiciary except in these specific areas.

Key Terms
حدود (hudud): fixed punishments for crimes against God (e.g., theft, zina, drinking)
قصاص (qisas): retaliation for bodily harm; equitable punishment
حدیث مرسل (hadith mursal): A hadith where the Companion is omitted; a Tabi'i reports directly from the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the evidentiary basis for excluding women from judging hudud and qisas?
A) Quranic verse 2:282
B) A mursal hadith that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud
C) Consensus of the Sahaba
D) Qiyas with inheritance

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits female judges except in hudud and qisas, based on a mursal hadith limiting women's testimony in those cases, and the Shafi'i disagreement is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

6 min
Letter of One Judge to Another Acceptable with Witnesses
Ruling on the validity of a judge's letter to another judge in rights cases when witnessed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a judge's letter to another judge is accepted in rights cases.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is accepted only when witnessed by two witnesses before the receiving judge.

In the Hanafi legal system, written correspondence between judges is a recognized means of transmitting judicial information. However, to prevent forgery and ensure authenticity, the Shariah imposes a strict evidentiary requirement: the letter must be formally witnessed. This lesson examines that condition and its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: the act of one judge sending a letter to another judge regarding legal rights (huquq).
2
Extract the legal condition
Identify the condition for acceptance: the letter must be witnessed by two witnesses before the receiving judge (shahada).
The phrase 'إذا شهد به عنده' means 'when it is witnessed before him'.
3
Note the scope of applicability
Understand that this ruling only applies to rights cases (huquq), not to hudud or qisas penalties.
Rights cases include financial claims and other civil matters.
4
Contrast with other schools
Compare with the Shafi'i position, which may require additional verification or not accept written correspondence without oral testimony.
The Hanafi position is relied upon in most Hanafi jurisdictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢٩١٢] (۲۵) ويقبل كتاب القاضي الى القاضي في الحقوق اذا شهد به عنده.
ایک قاضی کا خط دوسرے قاضی کے نام حقوق میں مقبول ہے جب خط کی گواہی اس کے سامنے دے۔
And the letter of a judge to a judge is accepted in rights when it is witnessed before him. One judge's letter to another judge is accepted in rights when the letter is testified before him.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage states a procedural ruling: the written correspondence of a judge sent to another judge regarding legal rights (huquq) is admissible provided that two witnesses testify before the receiving judge that the letter is indeed from the first judge. This ensures authenticity. The ruling applies to financial and other rights, not hudud or qisas.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي (kitab al-qadi): the formal written communication from one judge to another
شهد (shahida): to witness; in this context, to testify to the authenticity of the letter

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The sending judge must be present.
D) The letter must be in Arabic.

Key Takeaway

Kitab al-Qadi ila al-Qadi: Permissibility and Conditions
Ruling with proofs for kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi and identify the conditions under which a judge's letter is accepted.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is accepted except for hudud and qisas, provided the writing or seal is recognized.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on judicial correspondence. While Islamic procedure normally requires the defendant's presence, the school allows exceptions for administrative efficiency. The key issue is authentication: how does the receiving judge verify the letter's origin?

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi is permissible (ja'iz) except for hudud and qisas. Recognize the general permission and the specific exceptions.
2
Recognize the conditions for acceptance
The letter is accepted if the addressee judge recognizes the writing, or recognizes the seal, or witnesses testify to its authenticity. All three are alternative conditions.
3
Examine the first proof: hadith of the Prophet writing to Jews
The Prophet wrote to the Jews regarding the murder of Abdullah ibn Sahl. This establishes a precedent for written communication in judicial matters.
Bukhari, Bab Kitab al-Hakim ila Ummalihi
4
Examine the second proof: athar of Umar and statements of Ibrahim and al-Sha'bi
Umar wrote to his official about hudud, and Ibrahim said kitab al-qadi is permissible if writing and seal are recognized. This shows practice of Companions and Successors.
Bukhari, Bab al-Shahada ala al-Khatt al-Makhtum
5
Understand authentication via seal: hadith of the Prophet's seal ring
The Prophet adopted a silver seal ring because foreign rulers would not read unsealed letters. The seal serves as a means of identification.
If no authentication is possible, the letter must not be acted upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدود اور قصاص کے علاوہ جتنے حقوق ہیں ان میں ایک قاضی دوسرے قاضی کی طرف خط لکھے اور مکتوب الیہ قاضی کے سامنے گواہی دے کہ واقعی یہ خط فلاں قاضی کا ہے تو وہ خط مقبول ہے۔ اور جس قاضی کی طرف یہ خط لکھا ہے اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اس خط کے مطابق عمل کرے۔ کتاب القاضی الی القاضی کی دلیل کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ ان عبد الله بن سهل و محيصة خرجا الى خيبر ... فكتب رسول الله له اليهم به فكتب ماقتلناه (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب کتاب الحاکم الی عماله والقاضی الی امناءہ ص ۱۰۶۷، نمبر ۷۱۹۲ ) اس حدیث میں حضور نے حضرت عبداللہ بن سہل کے قتل پر یہود کو خط لکھا ہے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حاکم اپنے عمال کو خط لکھ سکتا ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ وقد كتب عـمـر الـى عـامـلـه في الحدود وقال ابراهيم كتاب القاضي الى القاضي جائز اذا عرف الكتاب والخاتم وكان الشعبي يجيز الكتاب المختوم بما فيه من القاضى (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الشهادة على الخط المحتوم و ما يجوز من ذلك و ما يضيق عليه، وكتاب الحاكم الى عماله والقاضی الی القاضی ، ص ۱۰۶۰ نمبر ۷۱۶۲ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر مکتوب الیہ قاضی کا تب قاضی کا خط اور مہر پہچانتا ہوتو وہ جائز ہے اور اس پر عمل کرنا جائز ہے۔ مکتوب الیہ قاضی جانتا ہو کہ یہ کا تب قاضی کا خط ہے یا کاتب قاضی کی مہر ہے یا کاتب قاضی کے بارے میں مکتوب الیہ قاضی کے سامنے گواہی دے کہ یہ فلاں کا خط ہے تب اس کے لئے عمل کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس کی دلیل اوپر کا اثر ہے۔ قال ابراهيم كتاب القاضي الى القاضي جائز اذا عرف الكتاب والخاتم (ج) (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک قال لما اراد النبي الله ان يكتب الى الروم قالوا انهم لا يقرؤن كتابا الا مختوما فاتخذ النبي الا الله خاتما من فضة كاني انظر الى وبيضه ونقشه محمد رسول الله (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشهادة على الخط المحتوم الخ ص۱۰۶۰ نمبر ۶۲ اے ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مہر بنائے کیونکہ مہر سے مکتوب الیہ قاضی جان سکتا ہے کہ یہ فلاں قاضی کا خط ہے (۳) اگر کسی قرینے سے یقین نہ ہو کہ یہ فلاں قاضی کا خط ہے تو مکتوب الیہ قاضی کیسے اس پر عمل کرے گا۔
Except for ḥudūd and qiṣāṣ, in all other rights, a judge may write a letter to another judge, and the addressee judge is given testimony that this letter is indeed from such-and-such judge – then that letter is accepted. And the judge to whom the letter is written has the option to act according to that letter. For the proof of kitāb al-qāḍī ilā al-qāḍī, this ḥadīth: 'Indeed ʿAbd Allāh ibn Sahl and Muḥayyiṣa went out to Khaybar... so the Messenger of Allāh wrote to them regarding it, and they wrote: We did not kill him' (Bukhārī, Bāb Kitāb al-Ḥākim ilā ʿUmmālihī, p. 1067, no. 7192). In this ḥadīth, the Prophet wrote to the Jews concerning the murder of ʿAbd Allāh ibn Sahl, from which it is known that a ruler can write to his officials. (2) There is an athar: 'ʿUmar wrote to his official concerning ḥudūd, and Ibrāhīm said: Kitāb al-qāḍī ilā al-qāḍī is permissible if the writing and the seal are recognized. And al-Shaʿbī allowed the sealed letter in what it contains from the judge' (Bukhārī, Bāb al-Shahāda ʿalā al-Khaṭṭ al-Makhtūm, p. 1060, no. 7162). From this athar it is known that if the addressee judge recognizes the writing and seal of the judge, it is permissible and acting upon it is permissible. If the addressee judge knows that it is the letter of the judge, or the seal of the judge, or testimony is given before the addressee judge that this is the letter of such-and-such, then it is permissible for him to act upon it. Its proof is the athar above: 'Ibrāhīm said: Kitāb al-qāḍī ilā al-qāḍī is permissible if the writing and the seal are recognized.' (3) In a ḥadīth: 'Anas ibn Mālik said: When the Prophet wanted to write to the Romans, they said: They will not read a letter unless it is sealed. So the Prophet took a seal ring of silver – as if I see its whiteness – and its engraving was Muḥammad the Messenger of Allāh' (Bukhārī, Bāb al-Shahāda ʿalā al-Khaṭṭ al-Makhtūm, p. 1060, no. 62A). This ḥadīth shows that a seal was made, because through the seal the addressee judge can know that this is the letter of such-and-such judge. (3) If there is no indication to give certainty that this is the letter of such-and-such judge, then how should the addressee judge act upon it?
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs concerning the legal concept of 'kitāb al-qāḍī ilā al-qāḍī' – a judge writing to another judge. The core ruling is that except for ḥudūd (fixed corporal punishments) and qiṣāṣ (retaliatory penalties), a judge may write to another judge regarding other rights and claims. The addressee judge may act on the letter if he recognizes the writing and seal, or if witnesses testify to its authenticity. The author provides three proofs: (1) a ḥadīth where the Prophet wrote to the Jews concerning a murder incident, establishing that a ruler can write to officials; (2) an athar from ʿUmar and Ibrāhīm al-Nakhaʿī stating that the practice is permissible if the writing and seal are recognized; (3) a ḥadīth about the Prophet's seal ring, which demonstrates the importance of a seal for authentication. The passage emphasizes that the addressee judge must have certainty through recognition or testimony; without that, he cannot act. This ruling is based on the principle of reliability and avoiding injustice.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي (kitāb al-qāḍī ilā al-qāḍī): A written correspondence from one judge to another regarding a legal case, particularly when the defendant resides in the second judge's jurisdiction.
الخط المختوم (al-khaṭṭ al-makhtūm): A sealed letter; the seal serves as authentication that the letter is from a specific judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The letter must be witnessed by two men or one man and two women.
B) The addressee judge must recognize the writing and seal of the sending judge.
C) The letter must be sent by a messenger who is a reliable Muslim.
D) The letter must be accompanied by oral testimony from the plaintiff.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a judge's letter to another judge for all cases except hudud and qisas, provided the receiving judge recognizes the writing or seal, or witnesses confirm it.

Judgment Requires a Present Defendant
States the ruling on judgment when witnesses testify before a present defendant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a Hanafi judge must pass judgment on testimony and explain the consequence if the condition is absent.

Core Idea
Judgment requires a present defendant—without presence, no verdict.

This lesson unpacks a concise procedural rule from the Hanafi fiqh of qada. When witnesses testify before a present defendant, the judge is obligated to pass judgment and also document his verdict. This rule safeguards the defendant's right to be heard. Understanding this condition is essential for the validity of judicial proceedings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the testimony of witnesses in court. When the defendant is present, it is wajib (obligatory) for the judge to pass judgment based on that testimony and to write his verdict.
The obligation arises only when the condition of presence is met.
2
Identify the condition
The key condition is the defendant's presence (khaṣm ḥāḍir). The text explicitly states that if the defendant is absent, the judge cannot pass judgment.
This protects the defendant's right to cross-examine and defend.
3
Understand the consequence of absence
When the defendant is absent, the judge must not render a verdict. Instead, if needed, he may use the kitāb al-qāḍī procedure to communicate with another judge for execution of a penalty, but only after a valid judgment has been passed.
The passage mentions that after judgment, the judge may write to another judge for execution of punishment.
4
Distinguish from kitāb al-qāḍī
The kitāb al-qāḍī procedure is separate: it allows a written testimony from one judge to be accepted by another, but the addressee judge has the option to act. The presence rule applies to initial judgment, not to execution.
This nuance is important to avoid confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۹۱۳] (۲۶) فان شهدوا على خصم حاضر حكم بالشهادة وكتب بحكمه. حدود اور قصاص کے علاوہ جتنے حقوق ہیں ان میں ایک قاضی دوسرے قاضی کی طرف خط لکھے اور مکتوب الیہ قاضی کے سامنے گواہی دے کہ واقعی یہ خط فلاں قاضی کا ہے تو وہ خط مقبول ہے۔ اور جس قاضی کی طرف یہ خط لکھا ہے اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اس خط کے مطابق عمل کرے۔ مدی علیہ مجلس قضا میں حاضر ہے ایسی صورت میں گواہی دی گئی تو گواہی پر حکم لگائے اور قاضی اپنا فیصلہ بھی لکھے گا۔ مدعی علیہ غائب ہو تو فیصلہ نہیں کر سکتا۔ اس لئے اگر مدعی علیہ حاضر ہو تو فیصلہ کرے گا۔ اس کے بعد کسی اور ضرورت مثلا سزادینے کے لئے - دوسرے قاضی کو بھیجنا پڑے تو بھیج دے۔
[2913] (26) If they testify against a present opponent, he passes judgment on the testimony and writes his verdict. Except for ḥudūd and qiṣāṣ, in all other rights, a judge may write to another judge, and the addressee judge is given testimony that this letter is indeed from such-and-such judge – then that letter is accepted. And the judge to whom the letter is written has the option to act according to that letter. The defendant is present in the court; when testimony is given in such a situation, he passes judgment on the testimony and the judge will also write his decision. If the defendant is absent, he cannot pass judgment. Therefore, if the defendant is present, he will pass judgment. After that, if there is another need, for example to execute a punishment, and it becomes necessary to send to another judge, he may send it.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This is a ruling statement (ḥukm) from the matn of the Sharḥ. The ruling is clear: when witnesses testify in the presence of the defendant (khaṣm ḥāḍir), the judge must pass judgment based on the testimony and also write down his verdict. This is because the defendant has the opportunity to defend himself. The commentary emphasizes that the defendant must be present in the court; if he is absent, the judge cannot render a verdict. The ruling also connects to the topic of kitāb al-qāḍī ilā al-qāḍī: if the defendant is found guilty and a penalty is to be executed in another jurisdiction, the judge may write to that judge to carry it out. This shows the integration of procedural rules for judgment and execution.

Key Terms
خصم حاضر (khaṣm ḥāḍir): The defendant who is present in the court at the time of testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He passes judgment on the testimony and writes his verdict.
C) He postpones the judgment until the defendant is absent.
D) He only writes the testimony but does not pass judgment.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi judge must pass judgment and write the verdict only when the defendant is present; absence invalidates the judgment.

Judgment on an Absent Defendant: Rule and Exception
Ruling on testimony in absence of defendant with proofs and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when witnesses testify without the defendant present and identify the exceptional case where judgment in absentia is permitted.

Core Idea
A judge must not rule on an absent defendant; he forwards testimony to the defendant's judge unless necessity allows judgment in absentia.

This lesson examines a fundamental principle of Islamic judicial procedure: the necessity of hearing both parties before passing judgment. The source passage presents the general rule—no judgment on an absent defendant—supported by the hadith of ʿAlī and the athar of Shurayḥ. It also introduces an important exception derived from the hadith of Hind, where the Prophet allowed a wife to take maintenance from her absent husband's wealth. Understanding this balance is crucial for applying the law correctly in courts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Read the opening line: 'If they testify in the absence of his opponent, he does not pass judgment but writes the testimony so that the addressee judge may judge by it.' This is the default rule: no judgment in absentia.
2
Understand the rationale
The reason given is that the absent defendant might have a valid defense. The judge must hear both sides to ensure justice (based on the hadith of ʿAlī).
3
Examine the proofs
Two proofs are cited: (1) The hadith where the Prophet instructed ʿAlī to hear from both opponents before judging. (2) The athar of Shurayḥ: 'Do not pass judgment on an absent person.' These establish the general prohibition.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud; the athar is from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Find the exception
Imam Bukhari cites the hadith of Hind: the Prophet allowed her to take maintenance from Abu Sufyan's wealth without him being present. This shows that when bringing the defendant is difficult and the claim is for a necessary right (like maintenance), judgment in absentia is permissible.
The Hanafi school accepts this exception but limits it to cases of genuine necessity.
5
Apply to a new scenario
If a plaintiff in City A claims a debt from a defendant in City B, and bringing him is very difficult, the judge should write the testimony and send it to the judge in City B. But if it is a maintenance claim (nafaqah), the judge may pass judgment in absentia due to the exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۱۴ (۲۷) وان شهدوا بغير حضرة خصمه لم يحكم وكتب بالشهادة ليحكم بها المكتوب اليه ۲۹۱۵ ۲۸ ) ولا يقبل الكتاب الا بشهادة رجلين او رجل وامرأتين. (۲۹۱۴) (۲۷) اور اگر گواہی دی مدعی علیہ کی غیر موجودگی میں تو فیصلہ نہ کرے بلکہ گواہی لکھ لے تا کہ مکتوب علیہ قاضی اس کا فیصلہ کرے۔ ایسی صورت ہے کہ گواہ حضرات ایک قاضی کے خطے میں ہیں اور مدعی علیہ دوسرے قاضی کے خطے میں ہے۔ اور دونوں کو جمع کرنا مشکل ہے ایسی صورت میں جس قاضی کے سامنے گواہ پیش ہوئے وہ قاضی گواہی لکھ لے۔ لیکن فیصلہ نہ کرے کیونکہ مدعی علیہ غائب ہو تو فیصلہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ گواہی مکتوب الیہ قاضی کو بھیج دے تا کہ وہ فیصلہ کرے اور مدعی علیہ پر نافذ کرے۔ غائب مدعی علیہ پر فی الہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کوئی ایسی بات کہے جس سے اس کے خلاف فیصلہ نہ ہو سکتا ہو ۔ اس لئے مدعی علیہ یا اس کا وکیل حاضر ہو تب فیصلہ کرے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت علی مو فر مایا کہ مدعی علیہ کی بات سن لو پھر فیصلہ کیا کرو۔ عن على قال بعثني رسول الله الله الله الى اليمن قاضيا ... فقال ان الله سيهدی قلبک ویثبت لسانک فاذا جلس بین یدیک الخصمان فلا تقضين حتى تسمع من الآخر كما سمعت من الاول فانه احرى ان يتبين لك القضاء (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب کیف القضاء، ص ۱۴۸، نمبر ۳۵۸۲ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی القاضی لا یقضی بین ا الخصمين حتى يسمع كلاهما ص ۲۴۸ نمبر (۱۳۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دوسرے کی بات سنوتب فیصلہ کرو اور یہ اسی وقت ہو سکتا ہے کہ مدعی علیہ یا اس کا وکیل حاضر ہو ( ۳) اثر میں ہے۔ قال سمعت شريحا يقول لا يقضى على غائب (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، بالا یقضی علی غائب، ج ثامن، ص ۱۳۰۴، نمبر ۱۵۳۰۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غائب پر فیصلہ نہ کرے۔ اس لئے صرف شہادت لکھ کر دوسرے قاضی کو بھیج دے تا کہ وہ فیصلہ کرے۔ اد امام بخاری فرماتے ہیں کہ مدعی علیہ کو حاضر کرنا مشکل ہو تو غائب مدعی علیہ کے خلاف بھی فیصلہ کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عائشة أن هندا قالت للنبي الله ان ابا سفيان رجل شحيح واحتاج ان اخذ من ماله ، قال له خذی ما یکفیک وولدك بالمعروف (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب القضاء علی الغائب میں ۱۰۶۴ نمبر ۷۱۸ ) اس حدیث میں حضرت سفیان حاضر نہیں تھے اس کے باوجود حضور نے اس کے مال سے مناسب نفقہ لینے کا فیصلہ فرمایا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قضا علی الغائب جائز ہے۔
[2914] (27) If they testify in the absence of his opponent, he does not pass judgment but writes the testimony so that the addressee judge may judge by it. [2915] (28) And the letter is not accepted except with the testimony of two men or one man and two women. (2914) (27) And if testimony is given in the absence of the defendant, then he should not pass judgment but rather write the testimony so that the addressee judge may judge by it. The situation is that the witnesses are in the jurisdiction of one judge, and the defendant is in the jurisdiction of another judge, and it is difficult to bring them together. In such a case, the judge before whom the witnesses appear should write the testimony. But he should not pass judgment because it is not permissible to pass judgment when the defendant is absent. And he should send this testimony to the addressee judge so that he may pass judgment and enforce it on the defendant. It is not permissible to pass judgment on an absent defendant because it may be that the defendant could say something that would prevent the judgment against him. Therefore, when the defendant or his representative is present, then pass judgment. (2) There is a hadith: ʿAlī said that the Messenger of Allāh sent him to Yemen as a judge... he said: 'Indeed Allāh will guide your heart and strengthen your tongue. When two opponents sit before you, do not pass judgment until you hear from the other as you heard from the first, for that is more likely to make the judgment clear to you.' (Abū Dāwūd, Bāb Kayf al-Qaḍā, p. 148, no. 3582; Tirmidhī, Bāb Mā Jāʾa fī al-Qāḍī Lā Yaqḍī, p. 248, no. 133). This hadith instructs to hear the other side, which is only possible when the defendant or his representative is present. (3) There is an athar: Shurayḥ said: 'Do not pass judgment on an absent person.' (Muṣannaf ʿAbd al-Razzāq, Bāb Lā Yaqḍī ʿalā Ghāʾib, vol. 8, p. 1304, no. 15306). This athar shows that one should not pass judgment on an absent person. Therefore, only write the testimony and send it to the other judge so that he may pass judgment. Imām Bukhārī says: If bringing the defendant is difficult, judgment may be passed against an absent defendant. There is proof in the hadith: ʿĀʾishah said that Hind said to the Prophet, 'Abū Sufyān is a stingy man, and I need to take from his wealth.' He said, 'Take what suffices you and your child in a reasonable manner.' (Bukhārī, Bāb al-Qaḍāʾ ʿalā al-Ghāʾib, p. 1064, no. 718). In this hadith, Abū Sufyān was not present, yet the Prophet passed judgment to take from his wealth for maintenance. From this it is known that judgment on an absent person is permissible.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding witnesses testifying in the absence of the defendant. The core ruling is that if the defendant is in a different jurisdiction and it is difficult to gather all parties, the first judge should not pass judgment but should write down the testimony and send it to the judge in whose jurisdiction the defendant resides. The reason is that the absent defendant must be heard to ensure justice. The author provides two proofs: (1) The famous hadith of ʿAlī where the Prophet instructed him to hear both sides before judging. (2) The athar of Shurayḥ stating explicitly 'do not pass judgment on an absent person.' However, the author also notes that Imām Bukhārī allows judgment on an absent person when bringing him is difficult, citing the hadith of Hind and Abū Sufyān. This apparent conflict is resolved by recognizing that the ruling of the first part applies when it is possible to bring the defendant, but if it is difficult, the Hanafi school allows judgment in absentia. The passage is thorough in presenting both sides and the evidence.

Key Terms
غائب (ghāʾib): An absent defendant who is not present in the court when witnesses testify.
مکتوب الیہ (maktūb ilayh): The addressee judge to whom the testimony is sent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the primary ruling in this passage, what should a judge do if witnesses testify in the absence of the defendant?
A) Pass judgment immediately based on the testimony.
B) Summon the defendant and then pass judgment.
C) Write the testimony and send it to the judge in the defendant's jurisdiction.
D) Dismiss the case due to the defendant's absence.

Key Takeaway
The default rule is that judgment on an absent defendant is prohibited; however, in cases of genuine difficulty, especially for maintenance claims, it may be allowed as an exception.

Proof Requirements for Acceptance of the Judge's Letter
States the evidentiary requirement for accepting a judge's letter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the standard of proof required to authenticate a judge's letter and identify the condition for its acceptance.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is accepted only upon the testimony of two men or one man and two women.

In Islamic judicial procedure, when a judge writes to another judge, the letter itself is not automatically accepted. It must be authenticated by witnesses. This lesson explains the required level of proof for the letter to be acted upon, which mirrors the standard evidence rules for financial claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is accepting a judge's letter. The ruling is that it is not accepted without witness testimony — the testimony is a condition (shart).
2
State the required testimonial standard
The text specifies two male witnesses OR one male and two female witnesses. This aligns with Hanafi rules for financial matters.
3
Understand why this condition exists
Without testimony, the authenticity of the letter is uncertain. Testimony provides verification, ensuring the letter genuinely comes from the issuing judge.

This is a brief but important ruling regarding the authentication of a judge's letter (kitāb al-qāḍī ilā al-qāḍī). The ruling states that the letter is not accepted as evidence unless it is accompanied by the testimony of two male witnesses, or one male and two female witnesses. This follows the general rule of evidence in Islamic law, where financial and property claims require two male witnesses or one male and two females. Note that this applies to the letter itself; the testimony confirms the authenticity of the letter. This ruling ensures that the letter meets the standard evidentiary threshold before the addressee judge can act upon it.

Judgment in Absentia: Writing Testimony for Another Judge
Ruling on testimony in defendant's absence and writing to another judge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on judgment in absentia and explain the procedure of writing testimony to another judge, including the evidence and the differing view of Imam Bukhari.

Core Idea
A judge does not rule in absentia; he writes testimony for the defendant's judge.

In Islamic judicial procedure, a fundamental principle is that a judgment should not be passed without hearing both parties. This lesson examines a specific case where witnesses testify in the presence of a judge but the defendant is in another jurisdiction. The Hanafi school prescribes a practical solution: the judge writes the testimony and sends it to the defendant's judge, rather than ruling in absentia. We will explore the proof for this ruling and a notable disagreement with Imam Bukhari.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: when witnesses testify without the defendant, the judge does not pass judgment but writes the testimony for the other judge.
The matn says: 'لم يحكم وكتب بالشهادة'.
2
Identify the proofs for the Hanafi position
Examine the hadith of Ali (ra) requiring hearing both sides and the athar of Shuraih prohibiting judgment against an absent person.
These are direct textual evidences.
3
Identify the opposing view
State Imam Bukhari's view that if summoning the defendant is difficult, judgment in absentia is permissible.
He cites the hadith of Hind and Abu Sufyan.
4
Analyze the practical difference
Explain the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi judges write to the defendant's judge; others may rule in absentia under necessity.
This affects judicial procedure.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the Hanafi position is the relied-upon view in the madhhab.
The matn and its proofs are considered stronger.

Source Text

اد امام بخاری فرماتے ہیں کہ مدعی علیہ کو حاضر کرنا مشکل ہو تو غائب مدعی علیہ کے خلاف بھی فیصلہ کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عائشة أن هندا قالت للنبي الله ان ابا سفيان رجل شحيح واحتاج ان اخذ من ماله ، قال له خذی ما یکفیک وولدك بالمعروف (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب القضاء علی الغائب میں ۱۰۶۴ نمبر ۷۱۸ ) اس حدیث میں حضرت سفیان حاضر نہیں تھے اس کے باوجود حضور نے اس کے مال سے مناسب نفقہ لینے کا فیصلہ فرمایا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قضا علی الغائب جائز ہے۔
And if they testify in the absence of his opponent, he shall not pass judgment but shall write the testimony so that the one written to may judge by it. (2914) (27) And if testimony is given in the absence of the defendant, do not pass judgment, rather write the testimony so that the judge written to may pass judgment on it. The situation is that the witnesses are in the jurisdiction of one judge and the defendant is in the jurisdiction of another judge, and it is difficult to bring them together. In such a case, the judge before whom the witnesses appear writes the testimony but does not pass judgment because passing judgment in the absence of the defendant is not permissible. And he sends this testimony to the judge written to so that he may pass judgment and enforce it against the defendant. Passing judgment against an absent defendant is not permissible because it is possible that the defendant might say something that would prevent judgment against him. Therefore, when the defendant or his agent is present, then pass judgment. (2) There is a hadith that Sayyiduna Ali said: Hear the statement of the defendant, then pass judgment. He said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sent me as a judge to Yemen... He said: Indeed Allah will guide your heart and establish your tongue. When the two litigants sit before you, do not judge until you hear from the other as you heard from the first, for that is more likely for you to clarify the judgment. (a) (Abu Dawud, Bab Kayf al-Qada, p. 148, no. 3582 / Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-qadi la yaqdi bayna al-khasmayn hatta yasma'a kalahuma, p. 248, no. 133) This hadith indicates that you should hear the other side and that is only possible when the defendant or his agent is present. (3) There is an athar: He said: I heard Shuraih say: No judgment is passed against an absent person. (b) (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab la yaqdi 'ala gha'ib, vol. 8, p. 1304, no. 15306) This athar shows that judgment is not passed against an absent person. Therefore, he merely writes the testimony and sends it to the other judge so that he may judge. And Imam Bukhari says that if bringing the defendant is difficult, then judgment may be passed against the absent defendant. There is proof for this in the hadith. From 'A'isha that Hind said to the Prophet: Abu Sufyan is a miserly man, and I need to take from his wealth. He said: Take what suffices you and your child in a reasonable manner. (c) (Bukhari, Bab al-Qada' 'ala al-gha'ib, p. 1064, no. 718) In this hadith, Abu Sufyan was not present, yet the Prophet passed judgment to take appropriate maintenance from his wealth. This shows that judgment against an absent person is permissible.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Adab al-Qadi (Etiquette of the Judge) section. It states that when witnesses testify in the absence of the defendant, the judge should not pass judgment but instead write down the testimony and send it to the judge who has jurisdiction over the defendant. The reason is that passing judgment in absentia is not permissible because the defendant might have a valid defense. The passage provides proofs: a hadith from Ali (ra) emphasizing hearing both sides, and an athar from Shuraih prohibiting judgment against an absent person. It then mentions a differing view from Imam Bukhari, who allows judgment in absentia if bringing the defendant is difficult, citing the hadith of Hind. The Hanafi position relied upon is the first view, as it aligns with the matn and the cited proofs.

Key Terms
کتاب القاضی الی القاضی (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written testimony sent from one judge to another judge when witnesses testify in the jurisdiction of the first judge but the defendant is in the jurisdiction of the second.
شہادت علی الشہادہ (shahadat 'ala al-shahada): Testimony upon testimony, i.e., witnesses testifying to the fact that a previous testimony was given. Here, it is used analogously for the written letter being a form of transferred testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi judge does not rule in absentia; he writes the testimony for the defendant's judge to ensure both sides are heard.

Acceptance of Written Testimony Requires Two Witnesses
Condition for accepting written testimony from another judge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for accepting a written testimony (kitab al-qadi) and explain the legal basis by analogy to transfer of testimony (naql al-shahada).

Core Idea
A judge's letter is only accepted when attested by two witnesses, because it is a transfer of testimony.

In this passage, we learn that a written communication from one judge to another (kitab al-qadi) is treated as a form of transferred testimony (naql al-shahada). The Hanafi school requires the same number of witnesses for such a letter as for testimony upon testimony: two men or one man and two women. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the proof from athar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the acceptance of a written testimony (letter) from one judge to another. The ruling is that it is not accepted unless attested by witnesses.
2
Classify the act legally
The letter is considered a form of transfer of testimony (naql al-shahada). Recall that naql al-shahada requires two witnesses for acceptance.
Analogically, the same requirement applies here.
3
Apply the prior ruling on naql al-shahada
Since the letter is akin to naql al-shahada, it requires two male witnesses or one male and two female witnesses to be accepted.
This is the Hanafi position.
4
Examine the dalil
The passage cites an athar from al-Sha'bi: 'Testimony of a witness upon a witness is not permissible until they are two.' This directly supports the requirement of two witnesses for testimony upon testimony.
The dalil is a Sunnah ahad (athar) with zanni thubut and zanni dalala.
5
Consider the additional reason
Handwriting can be similar, so witnesses are needed to ensure authenticity and remove doubt.
This reinforces the need for testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقبل الكتاب الا بشهادة رجلين او رجل وامرأتين (۲۹۱۵) (۲۸) مکتوب علیہ قاضی کے سامنے دو مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں گواہی دیں کہ یہ خط فلاں قاضی کا ہے تب مکتوب الیہ قاضی اس کو قبول کرے۔ یہ خط حقیقت میں نقل شہادت کے درجے میں ہے اور اوپر گزرا کہ نقل شہادت کے لے دو گواہی چاہئے اس لئے خط کے لئے بھی دو مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی چاہئے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ واول من سأل علی کتاب القاضي البينة ابن ابی لیلی وسوار بن عبد الله (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشهادة على الخط المحتوم الخ میں ۱۰۶۰ نمبر ۱۶۲ے ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ابن ابی لیلی اور سوار بن عبداللہ نے کتاب القاضی الی القاضی پر گواہ مانگا (۲) اور نقل گواہی پر دو گواہ چاہئے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن الشـعـبـي قــالا لاتجوز شهـادة الشاهد على الشاهد حتى يكونا اثنين (ب) (سنن بیہقی ، باب ما جاء في عدد شهو والفرع ، ج عاشر ص۲۲۴ نمبر ۲۱۱۹ رمصنف ابن ابى شيبة ، ۳۸۰ في شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد ، ج رابع ، ص ۵۵۴، نمبر ۲۳۰۷۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شھادۃ علی الشہادۃ کے لئے دو گواہ چاہئے۔ اور کتاب القاضی الی القاضی بھی ایک قسم کی نقل شہادت ہے اس لئے اس خط پر بھی دو گواہ چاہئے (۳) ایک کی تحریر دوسرے کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے اس لئے بھی یقین ہو جائے کہ یہ فلاں قاضی کا خط ہے اور اشتباہ باقی نہ رہے اس لئے بھی گواہی چاہئے۔
And the letter is not accepted except with the testimony of two men or one man and two women. (2915) (28) Before the judge written to, two men or one man and two women testify that this letter is from such-and-such judge, then the judge written to accepts it. This letter is in reality akin to transfer of testimony (naql al-shahada), and it has passed earlier that transfer of testimony requires two testimonies. Therefore, for the letter also, two men or one man and two women's testimony is required. (2) There is an athar: The first to ask for evidence (bayyinah) on the letter of a judge to a judge were Ibn Abi Layla and Sawwar ibn 'Abd Allah. (a) (Bukhari, Bab al-Shahada 'ala al-Khatt al-Makhtum, p. 1060, no. 162?) This athar indicates that Ibn Abi Layla and Sawwar ibn 'Abd Allah demanded witnesses for the letter of a judge to a judge. (2) And for testimony upon testimony, two witnesses are required. The proof for this is the following athar: From al-Sha'bi who said: Testimony of a witness upon a witness is not permissible until they are two. (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab ma ja'a fi 'adad shuhud al-far', vol. 10, p. 224, no. 2119; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 380 in Kitab al-Shahadat 'ala al-Shahada, vol. 4, p. 554, no. 23070) This athar shows that for testimony upon testimony, two witnesses are required. And the letter of a judge to a judge is also a type of transfer of testimony, therefore two witnesses are required for this letter. (3) One person's handwriting may resemble another's, so this is also why testimony is required so that it becomes certain that this is the letter of such-and-such judge, and no doubt remains.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that a written testimony (kitab al-qadi) sent from one judge to another is only accepted when it is attested by two male witnesses or one male and two female witnesses. The reason is that this letter is considered a transfer of testimony (naql al-shahada), which requires two witnesses. The passage cites an athar that Ibn Abi Layla and Sawwar ibn 'Abd Allah were the first to require evidence on such letters, and another athar from al-Sha'bi that testimony upon testimony requires two witnesses. Additionally, it notes that handwriting can be similar, so witnesses are needed to confirm the authenticity of the letter.

Key Terms
نقل شہادت (naql al-shahada): Transfer of testimony; when witnesses testify that a previous testimony was given elsewhere. Here, the written letter is treated as a form of transferred testimony.
کتاب القاضی الی القاضی (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written communication from one judge to another containing testimony or a legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why does a written testimony (kitab al-qadi) require two male witnesses or one male and two female witnesses?
A) Because it is a form of testimony upon testimony (naql al-shahada)
B) Because judges are not trustworthy
C) Because it is a contract
D) Because the Quran requires it

Key Takeaway
A judge's letter is accepted only when attested by two witnesses, as it is a transfer of testimony requiring the same proof as original testimony.

Judge Must Read Written Testimony to Witnesses Before Sealing
Procedure for sending written testimony: reading to witnesses, sealing, and handing over.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the procedure for sending written testimony and explain the proof from athar.

Core Idea
A judge must read the letter to witnesses before sealing so they know its contents; testimony without knowledge is invalid.

This passage outlines the procedural requirement for a judge when writing a testimony to be sent to another judge. It is obligatory (wajib) for the judge to read the letter to the witnesses who will carry it, so they know its contents. Then he must seal it and hand it to them. The purpose is to ensure that the witnesses can accurately testify before the second judge, and that their testimony matches the contents of the letter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge's procedure for sending written testimony. The ruling is: wajib (obligatory) to read the letter to the witnesses before sealing and handing over.
The passage explicitly states 'ويجب' (and it is necessary).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar: from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that a sealed will must be read to witnesses before they testify. Also Hasan al-Basri and Abu Qilaba disapproved testifying without knowledge.
The athar is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi, cited in the text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition of testifying without reading or hearing the document establishes the requirement of knowledge of contents. The judges' letter is analogous to a will: both require witnesses to know the contents.
The ruling is derived by qiyas from the will case.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some may think that seeing the sealed document is sufficient. The Hanafi view rejects this, requiring actual knowledge through reading.
This is the common misunderstanding listed.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The athar is relied upon as sound practice. The Hanafi school adopts this as the mufta bihi position.
The footnote mentions that testimony upon testimony is valid with two witnesses.

ويجب ان يقرأ الكتاب عليهم ليعرفوا مافيه ثم يختمه ويُسلّمه اليهم (۲۹۱۶) (۲۹) کا تب قاضی پر ضروری ہے کہ لے جانے والے گواہوں کے سامنے خط پڑھے تاکہ وہ جان لیں کہ خط میں کیا لکھا ہوا ہے۔ اور مکتوب الیہ قاضی کے سامنے گواہی دینے میں آسانی ہو۔ پھر خط پر مہر لگا کر گواہوں کے حوالے کرے تا کہ مکتوب الیہ قاضی کو خط دے سکے۔ گواہوں کے سامنے تو اس لئے پڑھے کہ وہ یادر کھے کہ خط میں مضمون کیا ہے تا کہ مکتوب الیہ قاضی کے سامنے اس کی گواہی دے سکے تاکہ خط کا مضمون اور گواہی ایک طرح کے ہوں (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ وکره الحسن وابو قلابة ان يشهد على وصية حتى يعلم ما فيها لانه لايدرى لعل فيها جورا(ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشہادة على الخط المحتوم الخ ص۱۰۶۰، نمبر ۷۱۶۲ رسن للبیہقی ، باب الاحتیاط فی قراءة الكتاب والاشهاد عليه وختمه اصلا نیز در علیه، ج عاشر ص ۲۱۹، نمبر ۲۰۴۱۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جب تک جان نہ لے کہ خط میں کیا ہے گواہی نہ دے (۳) عن ابراهيم في الرجل يختم على وصيته وقال اشهدوا على ما فيها قال لايجوز حتى يقرأها او تقرأ عليه فيقر بما فيها (و) سنن لليبقى ، باب الاحتیاط في قراءة الكتب والاشهاد عليه و حتمه لا یز در علیه ج عاشر ص ۲۲۰ نمبر ۲۰۴۲۰) اس اثر حاشیہ : (الف) کتاب القاضی پر سب سے پہلے ابن ابی لیلی اور سوار بن عبد اللہ نے بینہ مانگا (ب) حضرت مفتی نے فرمایا شہادۃ علی الشہادة جائز ہے یہاں تک کہ دو شاہد ہوں (ج) حضرت حسن اور ابو قلابہ نے نا پسند فرمایا کہ کسی کی وصیت پر گواہی دے یہاں تک کہ جان لے کہ اس میں کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس میں ظلم ہو (1) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی اپنی وصیت پر مہر لگائے۔ فرمایا اس میں کیا ہے، اس پر گواہ بنا ؤ، فرمایا نہیں جائز ہے یہاں تک کہ اس کو پڑھے یا اس پر پڑھائے اور جو کچھ اس میں ہے ثابت کرے۔
And he must read the letter to them so they know what is in it, then seal it and hand it over to them. (2916) (29) It is necessary for the judge that he read the letter before the witnesses who are to carry it so that they know what is written in it, and to make it easy for them to testify before the judge written to. Then he seals the letter and hands it over to the witnesses so that they can give the letter to the judge written to. He reads it before the witnesses so that they remember what is in the letter, so that they can testify to it before the judge written to, and so that the contents of the letter and the testimony are consistent. (2) There is an athar: Hasan and Abu Qilaba disapproved testifying to a will until one knows what is in it, because one does not know, perhaps there is injustice in it. (c) (Bukhari, Bab al-Shahada 'ala al-Khatt al-Makhtum, p. 1060, no. 7162; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Ihtiyat fi Qira'at al-Kitab wa al-Ishhad 'alayhi wa Khatmih, vol. 10, p. 219, no. 20419) This athar shows that one should not testify until he knows what is in the letter. (3) From Ibrahim regarding a man who seals his will and says: Make witnesses to what is in it. He said: It is not permissible until he reads it or it is read to him and he acknowledges what is in it. (d) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Ihtiyat fi Qira'at al-Kutub wa al-Ishhad 'alayhi wa Khatmih, vol. 10, p. 220, no. 20420) This athar... Footnotes: (a) Ibn Abi Layla and Sawwar ibn 'Abd Allah were the first to ask for evidence on a judge's letter. (b) The mufti said: Testimony upon testimony is permissible up to two witnesses. (c) Hasan and Abu Qilaba disapproved testifying to a will until he knows what is in it because perhaps there is injustice. (d) Ibrahim said: A man sealed his will, and he said: Make witnesses to what is in it. He said: Not permissible until he reads it or it is read to him, and he affirms what is in it.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage outlines the procedural requirement for a judge when writing a testimony to be sent to another judge. It is obligatory (wajib) for the judge to read the letter to the witnesses who will carry it, so they know its contents. Then he must seal it and hand it to them. The purpose is to ensure that the witnesses can accurately testify before the second judge, and that their testimony matches the contents of the letter. The passage supports this with athar: Hasan al-Basri and Abu Qilaba disapproved testifying to a will without knowing its contents, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i stated that a will must be read before witnesses. The footnotes provide further context, including that Ibn Abi Layla and Sawwar were the first to require evidence on such letters, and that testimony upon testimony is valid with two witnesses.

Key Terms
مہر (muhr): Seal used by the judge to authenticate the letter after it has been read to the witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) So they can memorize it for themselves
B) So they know its contents and can testify accordingly before the second judge
C) To check for errors
D) To entertain the witnesses

Key Takeaway
A judge must read the letter to the witnesses before sealing to ensure they know its contents; this is wajib and based on athar.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

The Obligation of Reading and Sealing the Qadi's Letter with Witnesses
Ruling with proof on reading and sealing a qadi's letter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a qadi's letter requires two witnesses, explain the analogy to transfer of testimony, and identify the proofs from athar and hadith.

Core Idea
A qadi's letter is a transfer of testimony; it requires two witnesses to be valid.

In the Hanafi judiciary, when a qadi sends a written order to another qadi, the letter must be handled with care to ensure its authenticity. The text before us lays out two obligations: reading the letter to the witnesses and sealing it. The deeper legal reasoning classifies the letter as a form of transfer of testimony (naql shahada), thus requiring the same number of witnesses. This lesson will unpack the proofs from the early scholars and the Prophet's practice, showing how this ruling safeguards justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its wajib status
Observe the explicit word 'يجب' (it is obligatory). The commentator treats this as wajib, not fard, because the evidences are from ahad athar, not mutawatir. Confirm the hukm level from the hanafi_position_box.
This is a procedural obligation for the qadi.
2
Understand the analogy to naql al-shahada
The letter is analogous to testimony upon testimony (shahada ala al-shahada), because the witnesses convey what is written. Since testimony on testimony requires two witnesses, so does the letter. Trace the qiyas: asl = transfer of testimony; far' = qadi's letter; illa = need for certainty in transmission.
The commentator explicitly states: 'هذا خط حقیقت میں نقل شہادت کے درجے میں ہے'.
3
Examine the textual proofs (athar and hadith)
The commentator cites three key proofs: (1) Athar from al-Sha'bi that 'testimony on a witness is not valid until they are two', (2) Practice of Ibn Abi Layla and Sawwar ibn Abdullah who first required witnesses for a qadi's letter, (3) Hadith of Anas about the Prophet's seal. For each, identify the specific wording that supports the ruling.
The hadith on sealing is used to establish the Sunnah of sealing, but the main ruling on witnesses is from the athar and analogy.
4
Analyze the purpose of reading to the witnesses
The reading ensures the witnesses know the contents so they can testify accurately before the addressee qadi. The commentator cites athar from Hasan al-Basri and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i emphasizing that one must not testify without knowledge. This prevents false testimony and ensures the testimony matches the letter.
This step connects the obligation to a broader principle of testifying only with certainty.
5
Understand the reason for sealing
Sealing serves two purposes: following the Prophet's practice (making a silver ring with 'Muhammad Rasulullah' engraved) and preventing tampering. The hadith of Anas is used as direct evidence. The seal guarantees the letter's integrity end to end.
The seal is not just a formality; it is a tool of authentication in an age without modern security.

اس لئے اس خط پر بھی دو گواہ چاہئے (۳) ایک کی تحریر دوسرے کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے اس لئے بھی یقین ہو جائے کہ یہ فلاں قاضی کا خط ہے اور اشتباہ باقی نہ رہے اس لئے بھی گواہی چاہئے۔ [۲۹۱۶] (۲۹) اور واجب ہے کہ گواہوں کے سامنے خط پڑھے تاکہ وہ جان لیں کہ خط میں کیا ہے، پھر اس پر مہر لگائے اور گواہوں کے سپرد کرے۔ کا تب قاضی پر ضروری ہے کہ لے جانے والے گواہوں کے سامنے خط پڑھے تاکہ وہ جان لیں کہ خط میں کیا لکھا ہوا ہے۔ اور مکتوب الیہ قاضی کے سامنے گواہی دینے میں آسانی ہو۔ پھر خط پر مہر لگا کر گواہوں کے حوالے کرے تا کہ مکتوب الیہ قاضی کو خط دے سکے۔ گواہوں کے سامنے تو اس لئے پڑھے کہ وہ یادر کھے کہ خط میں مضمون کیا ہے تا کہ مکتوب الیہ قاضی کے سامنے اس کی گواہی دے سکے تاکہ خط کا مضمون اور گواہی ایک طرح کے ہوں (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ وکره الحسن وابو قلابة ان يشهد على وصية حتى يعلم ما فيها لانه لايدرى لعل فيها جورا(ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشہادة على الخط المحتوم الخ ص۱۰۶۰، نمبر ۷۱۶۲ رسن للبیہقی ، باب الاحتیاط فی قراءة الكتاب والاشهاد علیه وختمه اصلا نیز در علیه، ج عاشر ص ۲۱۹، نمبر ۲۰۴۱۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جب تک جان نہ لے کہ خط میں کیا ہے گواہی نہ دے (۳) عن ابراهيم في الرجل يختم على وصيته وقال اشهدوا على ما فيها قال لايجوز حتى يقرأها او تقرأ عليه فيقر بما فيها (و) سنن لليبقى ، باب الاحتیاط في قراءة الكتب والاشهاد علیه و حتمه لا يز در علیه ج عاشر ص ۲۲۰ نمبر ۲۰۴۲۰) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ گواہ کو علم ہو کہ خط میں کیا ہے تا کہ جھوٹ گواہی نہ دے سکے۔ اور خط پر مہر لگائے اس کی دلیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ عن انس بن مالك قال لما اراد النبي الا الله ان يكتب الى الروم قالوا انهم لايـقـرون كتابا الا مختوما فاتخذ النبي الله خاتما من فضة كاني انظر الى وبيضه ونقشه محمد رسول الله (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشهادة على الخط المحتوم الخ ص۷۱۶۲/۱۰۶۰ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے مہر بنوائی تاکہ خط پر مہر لگائی جاسکے (۲) مہر لگانے سے خط میں کوئی کمی زیادتی نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے بھی مہر لگائے۔
It is obligatory to read the letter to them so that they know what is in it, then he should seal it and hand it over to them. The addressee qadi: two men or one man and two women should testify in front of him that this letter is from such-and-such qadi, then the addressee qadi should accept it. This letter is in reality a transfer of testimony, and it has passed earlier that for a transfer of testimony two witnesses are required. Therefore, for the letter also, two men or one man and two women are needed. There is an athar: 'The first to ask for proof regarding a qadi's letter were Ibn Abi Layla and Sawwar ibn Abdullah.' (Bukhari). From this athar it is known that Ibn Abi Layla and Sawwar ibn Abdullah asked for witnesses on the letter of a qadi to another qadi. For transfer of testimony, two witnesses are required; its evidence is this athar: From al-Sha'bi, he said: 'The testimony of a witness on a witness is not valid until they are two.' (Bayhaqi, Ibn Abi Shayba). From this athar it is known that for shahada ala al-shahada two witnesses are required. And the qadi's letter to a qadi is also a kind of transfer of testimony, so for this letter also two witnesses are required. Also, one person's handwriting resembles another's, so certainty is needed that this is the letter of such-and-such qadi and doubt is removed, so testimony is required. [2916] (29) And it is obligatory to read the letter in front of the witnesses so that they know what is in it, then seal it and entrust it to them. It is necessary for the writing qadi to read the letter in front of the witnesses who will carry it so that they know what is written in it, and so that it is easy for them to testify in front of the addressee qadi. Then he should seal the letter and hand it over to the witnesses so that they can deliver it to the addressee qadi. He reads it in front of the witnesses so that they remember what the content is, so that they can give testimony in front of the addressee qadi, so that the content of the letter and the testimony match. There is an athar: 'Hasan and Abu Qilaba disliked that one should testify on a will until he knows what is in it, because one does not know, perhaps there is injustice in it.' (Bukhari, Bayhaqi). From this athar it is known that one should not testify until he knows what is in the letter. From Ibrahim regarding a man who seals his will and says 'have witnesses on what is in it', he said: 'It is not permissible until he reads it or it is read to him and he affirms what is in it.' (Bayhaqi). From this athar it is also known that the witness should have knowledge of what is in the letter so that he cannot give false testimony. And the evidence for sealing the letter has passed before: from Anas ibn Malik, he said: 'When the Prophet (peace be upon him) wanted to write to the Romans, they said: They do not read a letter unless it is sealed. So the Prophet (peace be upon him) took a silver ring, I can still see its whiteness and its engraving Muhammad Rasulullah.' (Bukhari). In this hadith, he made a ring so that letters could be sealed. Also, sealing prevents anyone from adding or reducing anything in the letter, so he should seal it.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding the procedure for a qadi's letter (kitab al-qadi) sent to another qadi. The text is a commentary on the matn statement 'It is obligatory to read the letter to them...'. The commentator explains that the letter is treated as a transfer of testimony (naql shahada), therefore it requires the same number of witnesses: two men or one man and two women. He supports this with an athar that the first to require witnesses for such letters were the early judges Ibn Abi Layla and Sawwar ibn Abdullah. Further, he cites an athar from al-Sha'bi stating that testimony upon testimony requires two witnesses. The commentator then addresses the need to read the letter to the witnesses: this ensures they know its contents, avoid false testimony, and can accurately convey the content to the addressee qadi. He cites athar from Hasan al-Basri and Abu Qilaba, and from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, emphasizing that one must not testify until one knows the contents. Finally, he explains the reason for sealing: the Prophet's practice (using a seal) and to prevent tampering. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) based on the word 'يجب'. The proofs are from sunnah and athar, making it a well-established Hanafi position.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي (kitab al-qadi): A written order from one qadi to another, conveying a ruling or testimony.
شهادة على الشهادة (shahada ala al-shahada): Testimony of a witness who did not directly witness the event but heard it from another witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, why must a qadi read his letter to the witnesses before sealing it?
A) To ensure the witnesses memorize the content
B) To allow the witnesses to check for errors
C) So that the witnesses know its contents and can testify accurately before the addressee qadi
D) To prevent the letter from being lost

Key Takeaway
A qadi's letter is legally a transfer of testimony; it must be read to two witnesses and sealed to ensure authenticity and prevent fraud.

Accepting the Qadi's Letter Only in Presence of Opponent
Ruling on accepting the qadi's letter only in presence of opponent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a qadi must only accept a letter from another qadi in the presence of the defendant, and explain the proof from the hadith of Ali.

Core Idea
A qadi cannot enforce a letter of judgement without the defendant present — justice requires hearing both sides.

In Islamic judicial procedure, the principle of fair hearing is paramount. This lesson examines a specific scenario where a qadi receives a written judgement from another qadi. The short but decisive ruling states that he must not accept it — meaning enforce it — unless the defendant is present. The proof comes from a direct Prophetic instruction to Ali (ra) about the importance of hearing both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the addressee qadi receiving and enforcing a letter from another qadi. The ruling is that he should not accept it (for enforcement) except in the presence of the opponent (defendant).
The word 'لم يقبله' indicates prohibition of enforcement without the defendant.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that enforcement can only happen when the defendant is present, because the purpose of the letter is to apply a judgement.
Enforcement (نافذ) is the operative term.
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith narrated from Ali (ra) states: 'When the two opponents sit before you, do not judge until you hear from the other as you heard from the first.'
Abu Dawud, no. 3582; it is an ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut).
4
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'حتى تسمع من الآخر' (until you hear from the other) makes hearing the defendant a necessary condition before judgment. This implies the defendant must be present to be heard.
The imperative 'تسمع' indicates obligation (wujub) as per Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the ruling
When the addressee qadi receives a letter containing a judgement, he must summon the defendant and hear his response before enforcing the letter's content.
This ensures fairness and prevents injustice.
