And when it reaches the qadi, he should not accept it except in the presence of the opponent. The meaning of the letter reaching the addressee qadi is that he should make a judgement based on it and enforce it on the defendant. And enforcement can only happen when the defendant is present. Therefore, he should accept the letter in the presence of the defendant. In a hadith, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Ali: 'When the two opponents sit before you, do not judge until you hear from the other as you heard from the first, for that is more likely to clarify the judgement for you.' (Abu Dawud, no. 3582). From this hadith, it is understood that he should decide in the presence of the defendant.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the addressee qadi's procedure upon receiving a letter from another qadi. The matn states that he should not accept it except in the presence of the opponent (al-khasm, meaning the defendant). The commentator explains the reason: the purpose of the letter is to enforce a judgement, which can only be done when the defendant is present. He supports this with a hadith from the Prophet addressing Ali: a judge must hear both sides before deciding. This implies the defendant must be present to present his case. The ruling is based on the principle of fair hearing. The word 'لم يقبله' is interpreted as 'not accept for enforcement' rather than 'not receive'.

Key Terms
الخصم (al-khasm): The opponent in a case, specifically the defendant (مدعى عليه).

Procedure for Receiving the Qadi's Letter with Witnesses
Procedural conditions for enforcing a qadi's letter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the necessary conditions for a qadi to accept and enforce a letter from another qadi, and explain the rationale behind each step.

Core Idea
A qadi's letter is accepted only after verifying the seal and witness testimony to prevent fraud.

In judicial procedure, when a qadi receives a letter from another qadi via witnesses, he cannot simply open it. The Hanafi school outlines specific steps to ensure authenticity. This lesson unpacks those steps and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the addressee qadi's acceptance of a letter from another qadi. The ruling is that it is wajib to follow the prescribed procedure before enforcement.
The procedure is obligatory because it protects the rights of the opponent and ensures the letter is genuine.
2
List the conditions in order
First, inspect the seal for intactness. Second, the witnesses must testify that the sending qadi wrote, read, and sealed the letter in his court. Only then may the qadi open and enforce it.
The sequence is mandatory: seal check before testimony, testimony before opening.
3
Explain the rationale for each condition
The seal prevents tampering. The witness testimony confirms provenance. Together they establish authenticity of the document.
A broken seal immediately invalidates acceptance, regardless of testimony.
4
Identify the consequence of non-compliance
If any condition is missed, the qadi cannot enforce the letter. It must be resubmitted or returned to the sending qadi.
The opponent has the right to dispute the letter if procedure was not followed.
5
Note any further implications
The procedure balances efficiency and fairness. It also reflects the Hanafi emphasis on certainty (yaqin) in legal matters.
This procedure is part of qada (judicial) adab and is standard in Hanafi manuals.

And when the witnesses hand it over to him, he looks at its seal. Then if they testify that it is the letter of such-and-such qadi, and that he handed it over to us in his court and judgement session, and read it to us, and sealed it, then the qadi opens it, reads it to the opponent, and enforces what is in it. When the witnesses hand over the letter to the addressee qadi, the qadi first looks at its seal to see if it is intact or not. Because if the seal is broken, it means someone opened the letter and added or removed content. So first he checks the seal to see if it is intact. Then the witness gives testimony that such-and-such qadi wrote this letter in his court, handed it over to us, read it to us, and then sealed it. After these steps, the addressee qadi opens the letter, reads it to the opponent, and enforces its contents upon him. All these conditions are to ensure that this letter is indeed from that qadi. Then the purpose of the letter is that thing upon the opponent...

Commentary
This passage details the procedural steps for the addressee qadi when receiving a letter from another qadi. The ruling is from the matn, and the commentator explains each condition: first, check the seal for intactness; second, the witnesses must testify that the letter was written, read to them, and sealed in the sending qadi's court. Only after these verifications may the qadi open the letter, read it in the presence of the opponent, and enforce its contents. The rationale is to ensure authenticity and prevent fraud. The text does not cite explicit proof but is based on established practice and the earlier proofs about witnesses and sealing. This is a procedural ruling, and its authority weight is from the Hanafi tradition on judicial procedure.

Key Terms

Acceptance of a Judge's Letter Only in the Opponent's Presence
Ruling on when a judge may accept another judge's letter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a judge may accept a written judgment from another judge and explain the legal basis from the hadith.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is not enforceable until the defendant is present — fairness requires hearing both sides.

When a judge receives a written judgment from another judge, he may wish to implement it immediately. However, Hanafi law requires that the defendant be present. This rule ensures that both parties have an opportunity to be heard, as established by the Prophet's instruction to Ali (radiyallahu anhu). In this lesson, you will learn the precise condition and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? A judge receiving a letter from another judge. What is the ruling? He may not accept it except in the presence of the opponent (defendant).
The ruling is stated as a prohibition (لا يقبله) unless the condition is met.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud: the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) told Ali not to judge between two parties without hearing both sides.
The hadith is a direct command (فلا تقضين) implying the judge must hear both sides before deciding.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith establishes the principle that a judgment cannot be given without hearing the defendant. Since the letter implies a judgment against the defendant, the same principle applies: the defendant must be present to have the chance to respond.
The command 'لا تقضين' is understood as a prohibition of judging in absentia.
4
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
Suppose a judge in city A sends a letter to a judge in city B stating that Zayd owes money to Amr. If Zayd is not present before the judge in city B, the letter cannot be accepted or enforced.
The condition is strictly based on the defendant's presence, not just the plaintiff's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا وصل الى القاضى لم يقبله الا بحضرة الخصم

(۲۹۱۷ (۳۰) جب خط قاضی کے پاس پہنچے تو اس کو قبول نہ کرے مگر مدعی علیہ کے سامنے۔ مکتوب الیہ قاضی کے سامنے خط پہنچنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس پر وہ فیصلہ کرے اور مدعی علیہ پر نافذ کرے۔ اور نافذ کرنا اس وقت ہو سکتا ہے جب مدعی علیہ حاضر ہو۔ اس لئے مدعی علیہ کی حاضری میں خط قبول کرے۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت علی کو آپ نے فرمایا ۔ فماذا جلس بين يديك الخصمان فلا تقضين حتى تسمع من الآخر كما سمعت من الاول فانه احرى ان تبين لك القضاء (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب کیف القضاء، ص ۱۴۸، نمبر ۳۵۸۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مدعی علیہ حاضر ہو تب اس کے سامنے فیصلہ کرے۔
And when it reaches the judge, he does not accept it except in the presence of the opponent. (30) When the letter reaches the judge, he should not accept it except in the presence of the defendant. The meaning of the letter reaching the addressed judge is that he should decide based on it and enforce it upon the defendant. Enforcement can only occur when the defendant is present. Therefore, he should accept the letter in the presence of the defendant. In a hadith, the Prophet said to Ali: 'When the two opponents sit before you, do not judge until you hear from the other as you heard from the first, for it is more likely that the judgment will become clear to you.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 3582) From this hadith, it is understood that the defendant must be present before deciding.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on the etiquette of judges. It states that if a judge receives a written judgment from another judge (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi), he must not accept it and act upon it unless the defendant (al-khasm) is present. The reason is that enforcement of a judgment requires the presence of the defendant so that he can hear the ruling and respond if there is any contradiction. The commentator provides a hadith from the Prophet to Ali ibn Abi Talib, instructing him not to judge between two parties without hearing both sides. This hadith is used as proof that the judge must ensure both parties are present before implementing a judgment. This is a direct application of the principle of fairness in judicial proceedings. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, and there is no known intra-Hanafi dispute on this point.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written judgment or letter from one judge to another concerning a legal case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only when the defendant is present.
C) Only during formal court hours.
D) Only if the letter is delivered by the witnesses.

Key Takeaway
A judge may only accept and act upon another judge's written judgment in the presence of the defendant, as required by the principle of hearing both sides.

Procedure for Accepting a Sealed Letter from Witnesses
Conditions and procedure for accepting a judge's letter with witness testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for accepting a sealed letter from witnesses in a Hanafi court and identify the legal proof for sealing.

Core Idea
A sealed letter is only accepted if the witnesses testify that the judge wrote, read, and sealed it in his court.

In Islamic judicial procedure, written judgments may be transmitted via sealed letters. However, authenticity must be strictly verified. This lesson examines the Hanafi conditions for accepting such a letter and the prophetic precedent for sealing documents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge's acceptance of a sealed letter delivered by witnesses. The ruling is that the procedure described is wajib (obligatory); otherwise the letter is not enforceable.
2
Locate the dalil
The Hanafi school cites the hadith of the Prophet's seal from Sahih al-Bukhari to establish the importance of sealing documents to prevent forgery.
The hadith is ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The 'illa (effective cause) is prevention of tampering. This applies to judicial letters as much as to diplomatic correspondence, justifying the use of the hadith as proof.
This is an application of qiyas jali.
4
Apply the ruling
The judge must first check the seal's integrity, then require witnesses to testify that the issuing judge wrote the letter in his court, read it to them, and sealed it. Only then can he open and enforce the letter.
These conditions ensure authenticity and prevent false testimony.

And when the witnesses deliver it to him, he looks at its seal. And if they testify that it is the letter of such-and-such a judge, that he delivered it to us in his court of judgment and read it to us and sealed it, the judge opens it and reads it to the opponent and enforces what is in it. It is also understood from this that the witness must know what is in the letter so that he cannot give false testimony. Commentary
This passage details the procedure for accepting a written judgment delivered by witnesses. The judge must first verify the seal; if broken, the letter is suspect. Then the witnesses must testify to specific facts: that the issuing judge wrote the letter in his own court (majlis hukm), that he read it to them, and that he sealed it. This testimony establishes the authenticity of the letter. The hadith about the Prophet's seal from Sahih al-Bukhari is cited to show the importance of sealing documents. The seal prevents forgery. Once the letter is verified, the judge opens it, reads the contents to the opponent, and enforces the ruling. This procedure ensures both authenticity and fairness.

Judge May Not Appoint a Deputy Without Authorization
Ruling that a judge cannot appoint a deputy unless authorized.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a judge cannot appoint a deputy without the ruler's authorization, identify the proof from the hadith, and apply the qiyas analogy.

Core Idea
A judge cannot appoint a deputy without the ruler's permission — judicial authority is not delegable.

This lesson examines a fundamental rule of judicial administration: a judge does not have inherent authority to appoint a deputy to hear cases in his place. The appointment of judges is a prerogative of the head of state. However, if the ruler explicitly delegates this authority, the judge may appoint. The proof is drawn from a Prophetic hadith where the Prophet delegated the execution of a hadd penalty, illustrating that such delegation requires explicit authorization.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the general rule: the judge cannot appoint a deputy on his own authority.
The ruling applies to all types of judicial duties.
2
Identify the Exception
Note the exception: if the ruler (Amir al-Mu'minin) has authorized the judge to appoint a deputy, then it is permissible.
The authorization must be explicit and specific.
3
Locate the Dalil
Recall the hadith from Abu Huraira: the Prophet told Unais to go to the woman and, if she confesses, stone her.
This shows delegation of hadd execution requires specific permission.
4
Analyze the Qiyas
Compare the delegation of judicial appointment with delegation of hadd execution: both are acts of authority that require delegation from a higher authority.
The analogy (qiyas) justifies the ruling.
5
Apply the Ruling
Conclude that any judgment rendered by an unauthorized deputy is invalid and has no legal effect.
This protects the integrity of the judicial system.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس للقاضى ان يستخلف على القضاء الا ان يفوّض اليه ذلک

قاضی اپنی جگہ پر کسی کو قاضی بنانا چاہے تو نہیں بنا سکتا ، ہاں امیر المومنین نے ان کو اختیار دیا ہو کہ وہ اپنی جگہ قاضی بنا ئیں تو اب بنا سکتے ہیں۔

قاضی بنانا امیر المومنین کا کام ہے اس لئے وہی قاضی بنائیں گے۔ یا اس کی اجازت سے قاضی بنا سکیں گے (۲) جس طرح قاضی کسی کو حد جاری کرنے کا حکم دے تو وہ حد جاری کر سکتا ہے اسی طرح امیر قاضی کو قاضی بنانے کا اختیار دے تو وہ قاضی بنا سکتا ہے۔ حد جاری کرنے کے اختیار کی حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: واغد يا انيس الى امرأة هذا فان اعترفت فارجمها(ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الوکالۃ فی الحدود، ص ۱۳۱۱ نمبر ۲۳۱۴) اس حدیث میں آپ نے حضرت انس گور جم کرنے کا اختیار دیا تو وہ رجم کر سکے۔ يفوض : سپرد کرے۔
And it is not for the judge to appoint a deputy over judgment unless he is authorized to do so. (33) The judge cannot appoint someone as judge in his place. Yes, if the Amir al-Mu'minin has given him permission to appoint a judge in his place, then he can. Appointing a judge is the prerogative of the Amir al-Mu'minin, so he will appoint judges. Or he can appoint with his permission. Just as the judge can order someone to execute a hadd penalty, similarly the Amir can give the judge authority to appoint a judge. The hadith about executing hadd is: from Abu Huraira, the Prophet said: 'Go, O Unais, to this woman; if she confesses, then stone her.' In this hadith, the Prophet gave Unais the authority to stone.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This ruling establishes that a judge does not have inherent authority to appoint a deputy to act as judge in his place. The appointment of judges is the right of the head of state (Amir al-Mu'minin). However, if the ruler has explicitly delegated this authority to the judge, then he may appoint a deputy. The commentator draws an analogy with the authority to execute a hadd penalty: just as the Prophet delegated stoning to Unais, so the ruler can delegate judicial appointment. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الاستخلاف على القضاء (al-istikhlaf 'ala al-qada): Appointing a deputy to exercise judicial authority in one's place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can a judge appoint a deputy according to the Hanafi school?
A) He can always appoint a deputy.
B) He can appoint a deputy only with the permission of the Amir al-Mu'minin.
C) He can appoint a deputy only for criminal cases.
D) He can appoint a deputy if the deputy is more knowledgeable.

Key Takeaway
A judge's authority to appoint a deputy hinges on explicit authorization from the ruler; without it, the appointment is invalid.

Enforcement of Another Judge's Ruling
Ruling that a judge must enforce another judge's judgment unless it contradicts primary sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on enforcing another judge's judgment and identify the exceptions that allow non-enforcement.

Core Idea
A judge must enforce another judge's ruling unless it clearly contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, or is baseless.

This lesson introduces a key principle in Islamic judicial procedure: the obligation to respect and enforce rulings issued by other judges. The Hanafi school emphasizes finality and cooperation among courts, but allows non-enforcement only when a ruling clearly violates fundamental sources or is entirely without evidence. This rule ensures consistency and prevents arbitrary rejection of valid judgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the enforcement of another judge's ruling when it is brought before a judge. The ruling is that it must be enforced (wajib).
The obligation is on the judge, not on the parties.
2
List the conditions for enforcement
The ruling must be presented to the judge, and it must be a valid ruling from a qualified judge. The default is enforcement.
There is no condition that the ruling be from the same jurisdiction or madhhab.
3
Identify the exceptions (mawani)
Enforcement is withheld if the ruling contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or is a baseless opinion (i.e., without evidence).
These exceptions are narrow; mere disagreement with the ruling is insufficient.
4
Apply the rule
Given a scenario, determine whether any exception applies. If not, enforcement is obligatory.
The judge must have certainty of the contradiction; doubt does not justify non-enforcement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا رفع الى القاضي حكم حاكم امضاه الا ان يخالف الكتاب او السنة او الاجماع او

اگر لایا جائے قاضی کے پاس کسی حاکم کا حکم تو اس کو نافذ کر دے مگر یہ کہ قرآن کریم یا سنت یا اجماع کا مخالف ہو یا قول بغیر دلیل کے ہو۔
And if a ruling of a judge is brought to a (different) judge, he enforces it unless it contradicts the Book, the Sunnah, or consensus, or a baseless statement. (34) If a ruling of a judge is brought to a judge, he enforces it unless it is contrary to the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or a baseless opinion.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage establishes the principle of respect for judicial decisions (res judicata). A judge must enforce a valid judgment rendered by another judge, even if it is from a different jurisdiction, as long as it does not clearly contradict the primary sources of Islamic law (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma) or is not a baseless opinion (i.e., a ruling without evidence). This ensures finality and uniformity in the legal system. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is a cornerstone of judicial cooperation.

Key Terms
إمضاء الحكم (imda' al-hukm): Enforcement of a judicial ruling issued by another judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When must a judge refuse to enforce another judge's ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) When the ruling is from a different city.
B) When the ruling contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma.
C) When the ruling is unfavorable.
D) When the judge who issued it is of a different madhhab.

Key Takeaway
A judge must enforce another judge's ruling unless it clearly contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, or is a baseless statement.

Judge's Letter Not Accepted in Hudud and Qisas
Ruling that a judge's letter to another judge is not accepted in hudud and qisas cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting a judge's letter in hudud and qisas cases and explain the proof from the hadith of averting hudud.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is not accepted in hudud and qisas because hudud are averted by doubts, and a letter introduces doubt.

This passage presents the ruling that a judge's written communication to another judge is not accepted in hudud (fixed penalties) and qisas (retaliation) cases. The author provides three proofs: the famous hadith commanding to avert hudud as much as possible, the principle that hudud are dropped by doubts, and an athar from early scholars. Understanding this exception is crucial for judges and students of fiqh to apply the correct evidentiary standard in serious criminal cases.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act: accepting a judge's letter in hudud and qisas cases. State the ruling: it is not accepted (ghayr jā'iz).
2
Examine the first proof (hadith)
Read the hadith from Aisha (r.a.) where the Prophet ﷺ commands to avert hudud as much as possible. Understand that this command indicates a strong preference to avoid punishment when there is any doubt.
The hadith is a strong dalil for the principle of dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat.
3
Apply the principle of doubts
The letter of a judge introduces a potential doubt about the authenticity or accuracy of the claim. Since hudud are dropped by doubts, the letter cannot be used to execute a hadd.
This is the second proof mentioned in the text.
4
Consider the athar and cross-madhhab view
The athar from some early scholars states that a ruler's letter is permissible except in hudud, confirming the exception. Note that some other schools permit it in all cases, but the Hanafi school maintains the exception.
The Hanafi position is based on caution (ihtiyat) in matters of life and limb.
5
Summarize the operative ruling
The mufta bihi position is that a judge's letter to another judge is not accepted in hudud and qisas cases, but it is accepted in other cases like financial disputes.
This is consistent with the principle of averting hudud by doubts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[2919 (32)] ولا يقبل كتاب القاضى الى قاضي في الحدود والقصاص. (1) حدود اور قصاص کے بارے میں یہ ہے کہ حتی الامکان ان کو ساقط کرو۔ اور کتاب القاضی الی القاضی سے اور مضبوط ہو گا اس لئے کتاب القاضی الی القاضی حدود اور قصاص میں مقبول نہیں ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ادرء وا الحدود عن المسلمين ما استطعتم فان كان له مخرج فخلوا سبيله فان الامام ان يخطى في العفو خير من ان يخطى في العقوبة (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی درء الحدود، ص ۲۶۴، نمبر ۱۴۲۴ ردار قطنی، کتاب الحدود والدیات، ج ثالث ، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۰۷۵) (2) دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ حدود اور قصاص شبہات سے ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں اور کتاب القاضی الی القاضی میں شبہ ہوتا اس لئے بھی یہ حدود اور قصاص میں جائز نہیں ہو گا (3) اثر میں ہے۔ وقال بعض الناس كتاب الحاكم جائز الا في الحدود (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشهادة على الخط المحتوم الخ ص ۱۲۰ نمبر ۱۶۲ ) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ حدود میں کتاب القاضی الی القاضی جائز نہیں ہے۔
[2919 (32)] And a judge's letter to a judge is not accepted in hudud and qisas. (1) Regarding hudud and qisas, it is that they should be dropped as much as possible. And the letter of a judge to a judge would be stronger, therefore the letter of a judge to a judge is not accepted in hudud and qisas. The hadith is: From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Avert the hudud from the Muslims as much as you can; if there is a way out, then let him go free, for the imam to err in pardoning is better than to err in punishment.' (at-Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi dar' al-hudud, p.264, no.1424; ad-Daraqutni, Kitab al-hudud wa ad-diyat, vol.3, p.68, no.3075) (2) The second matter is that hudud and qisas are dropped by doubts, and in the letter of a judge to a judge there is doubt, therefore it is also not permissible in hudud and qisas. (3) There is an athar: 'And some people said: The letter of a ruler is permissible except in hudud.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab ash-shahada 'ala al-khat al-makhtum, p.120, no.162) This athar also indicates that a judge's letter to a judge is not permissible in hudud.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn: 'A judge's letter to another judge is not accepted in hudud and qisas.' The sharh expands with three proofs: First, the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ commanding to avert hudud as much as possible, showing that any doubt should lead to dropping the hadd penalty. The letter creates doubt about the authenticity of the claim, so it is not accepted. Second, hudud and qisas are dropped by doubts (shubuhat), and the letter itself introduces a doubt, thus it is not valid to execute a hadd based on it. Third, an athar from Bukhari cites that some scholars say the judge's letter is permissible except in hudud, confirming the exception. The Hanafi position is that such letters are not accepted in hudud and qisas to guard against possible error.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written communication from one judge to another regarding a legal case
حدود (hudud): Fixed penalties prescribed by the Quran and Sunnah for specific crimes (e.g., theft, zina, etc.)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a judge's letter not accepted in hudud and qisas according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the letter is not witnessed
B) Because hudud and qisas are dropped by doubts and the letter introduces doubt
C) Because the second judge does not have jurisdiction
D) Because the Prophet ﷺ prohibited writing letters

Key Takeaway
A judge's letter is not accepted in hudud and qisas because the Shariah commands to avert hudud by the slightest doubt, and the letter inherently introduces uncertainty.

Enforcing a Previous Judge's Ruling (Hukm al-Hakim)
Ruling that a judge must enforce a prior judgment unless it contradicts Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or is baseless

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on enforcing a prior judge's ruling and identify when rejection is required.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling is binding unless it contradicts Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma.

This lesson addresses a critical principle in Islamic judicial procedure: the finality and binding nature of a judge's decision (hukm al-hakim). The Hanafi school holds that a subsequent judge must enforce a previous ruling, but with a vital exception—if the ruling contradicts the primary sources of Sharia, it must be rejected. This balances respect for ijtihad and judicial stability with the supremacy of divine law.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the ruling from the matn: a judge presented with a previous judge's ruling must enforce it unless it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, or is a statement without evidence.
The default is enforcement.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Separate the case where the ruling is consistent with Sharia (enforce) from where it is contradictory (reject). Understand the rationale: consistency with Sharia means the ruling is valid and final; contradiction means it is void.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the athar from Shurayh ('I do not reject a ruling that was made before me') and the practice of al-Qasim ibn Abd al-Rahman enforcing Musa ibn Anas's ruling. Also consider the hadith 'Whoever innovates... it is rejected' as the basis for rejecting contradictory rulings.
These proofs establish the binding nature of prior rulings unless they conflict with definitive sources.
4
Apply the exception for opinion-based rulings
Understand the athar from al-Shu'bi: rulings contrary to Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma are rejected; rulings based on valid personal opinion (ra'y) are not rejected. This distinguishes between contradictions to primary sources and disagreements within ijtihad.
Personal opinion with evidence is permissible; only baseless opinions are rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[2921] (34) واذا رفع الى القاضي حكم حاكم امضاه الا ان يخالف الكتاب او السنة او الاجماع او يكون قولا لا دليل عليه. اس میں دو سکتے ہیں۔ ایک مسئلہ تو یہ ہے کہ پہلے قاضی کا فیصلہ قرآن، حدیث اور اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو تو مکتوب الیہ قاضی اس کو نافذ کرے گا۔ اور دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ قرآن، حدیث اور اجماع کے خلاف ہو تو اس فیصلے کو رد کر دے۔ (1) جب شریعت کے موافق ہے تو رد کرنے سے کیا فائدہ۔ کیونکہ پہلے قاضی کا بھی اجتہاد ہے اور اس قاضی کا بھی اجتہاد ہے۔ اور پہلے قاضی کے اجتہاد کے ساتھ فیصلہ بھی ہو چکا ہے اس لئے اس کو توڑنا اچھا نہیں ہے، نافذ کر دے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ حدثنا عبيد الله بن محرز جئت بكتاب من موسى بن انس قاضى البصرة واقمت عنده البينة ان لي عند فلان كذا وكذا وهو بالكوفة وجئت به القاسم بن عبد الرحمن فاجازه (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشہادة على الخط المحتوم الخ ص ۱۰۶۰، نمبر ۷۱۶۲) اس اثر: میں قاسم بن عبد الرحمن نے حضرت موسی بن انس کے فیصلے کو نافذ فرمایا (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن سيرين قال سمعت شريحا يقول اني لا ارد قضاء كان قبلی (ب) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب هل سرد قضاء القاضی؟ اور پرجمع عن قضاه ، ج ثامن ، ص ۱۳۰۲، نمبر ۱۵۲۹۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ خلاف شریعت نہ ہو تو ماقبل قاضی کے فیصلے کو رد نہیں کرنا چاہئے۔ اور قرآن ، حدیث یا اجماع کے خلاف ہو تو اس کو رد کر دے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله الا الله من احدث فی امرنا هذا ماليس فيه فهورد (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اصطلحو اعلی صلح جور فاصلح مردود ص ۳۷۱، نمبر ۲۶۹۷ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی لزوم السنته ، ج ۲، ص ۲۸۴، نمبر ۴۶۰۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شریعت میں نہ ہو تو مردود ہے۔ اس باب میں ایک دیہاتی کے بیٹے کے زنا کا واقعہ ہے۔ لوگوں نے ان کے لئے رجم کا فیصلہ کیا تو آپ نے اس کو رد فر مایا اور فرمایا کہ تمہارے بیٹے پر سو کوڑے ہیں کیونکہ وہ محسن نہیں ہے۔ (۳) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت خالد نے قیدیوں کے سلسلے میں قتل کا فیصلہ فرمایا جو شریعت کے خلاف تھا تو حضور نے اس کو رد فرمایا اور اس سے براءت ظاہر کی۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر بعث النبي قال لا اله خالدا ... فذكر نا ذلك للنبى الله الله فقال اللهم انى ابراء اليك مما صنع خالد بن الوليد مرتین (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا قضی الحاکم بجور او خلاف اہل العلم فحصور در ص ۱۰۶۶، نمبر ۷۱۸۹ ) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ خلاف شریعت فیصلہ ہو تو اس کو رد کیا جائے گا اور نافذ نہیں کیا جائے گا (۴) اثر میں اس کی صراحت ہے۔ عن الشورى قال اذا قضى القاضي بخلاف كتاب الله او سنة نبي الله او شيء مجتمع عليه ، فان القاضى بعده يرده ، فان كان شيئا براى الناس لم يرده ويحمل ذلك ما تحمل (ه) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب حل برد قضاء القاضی اور جمع عن قضاء ، ج ثامن، ص ۱۳۰۲ نمبر ۱۵۲۹۸)
[2921] (34) And if the ruling of a judge is brought before a judge, he shall enforce it unless it contradicts the Book, the Sunnah, the Ijma, or is a statement without evidence. In this there are two matters: one issue is that if the previous judge's ruling does not contradict the Quran, Hadith, and Ijma, then the judge to whom it is brought will enforce it. The second issue is that if it contradicts the Quran, Hadith, and Ijma, then he will reject that ruling. (1) When it is in accordance with Sharia, what benefit is there in rejecting it? Because the previous judge also has his ijtihad, and this judge also has his ijtihad. And the previous judge's ruling has already been made with his ijtihad, therefore breaking it is not good; he should enforce it. (2) There is an athar: 'Ubaydullah ibn Muhriz narrated: I came with a letter from Musa ibn Anas, the judge of Basra, and I established proof before him that so-and-so owed me such-and-such, and he was in Kufa. I brought it to al-Qasim ibn Abd al-Rahman, and he accepted it.' (Bukhari, Bab ash-shahada 'ala al-khat al-makhtum, p.1060, no.7162) In this athar, al-Qasim ibn Abd al-Rahman enforced the ruling of Musa ibn Anas. (3) There is an athar from Ibn Sirin who said: I heard Shurayh say: 'I do not reject a ruling that was made before me.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab hal yarudd qada al-qadi? wa jama' 'an qudah, vol.8, p.1302, no.15297) This athar indicates that if it does not contradict Sharia, the previous judge's ruling should not be rejected. And if it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, he will reject it. The hadith is: From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever innovates in this matter of ours something that is not from it, it is rejected.' (Bukhari, Bab idha istalahu 'ala sulh jawr fa al-sulh mardud, p.371, no.2697; Abu Dawud, Bab fi luzum al-sunnah, vol.2, p.284, no.4606). From this hadith, it is known that if something is not in Sharia, it is rejected. In this chapter, there is the incident of a bedouin's son and zina: the people decided on stoning for him, but the Prophet rejected it and said: 'Your son gets one hundred lashes because he is not muhsan.' (3) Another hadith: The Prophet sent Khalid, and when the killing of prisoners was mentioned before the Prophet, he said: 'O Allah, I disassociate myself from what Khalid ibn al-Walid did,' twice. (Bukhari, Bab idha qada al-hakim bi jawr aw khilaf ahl al-'ilm fahuwa mardud, p.1066, no.7189). This hadith also shows that if a ruling contradicts Sharia, it will be rejected and not enforced. (4) There is explicit athar from al-Shu'bi: 'If a judge rules contrary to the Book of Allah, or the Sunnah of His Prophet, or something unanimously agreed upon, then the subsequent judge rejects it. If it is something based on people's opinion, he does not reject it and bears it as much as he can.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab hal yarudd qada al-qadi wa jama' 'an qudah, vol.8, p.1302, no.15298)
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn: 'If the ruling of a judge is brought before a judge, he shall enforce it unless it contradicts the Book, the Sunnah, the Ijma, or is a statement without evidence.' The sharh expands by clarifying two scenarios. First, if the previous ruling is in accordance with Sharia, the second judge must enforce it out of respect for ijtihad and finality of judgment. Proofs include the practice of al-Qasim ibn Abd al-Rahman who enforced Musa ibn Anas's ruling, and the statement of Shurayh that he does not reject prior rulings. Second, if the ruling contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, it must be rejected. The hadith 'Whoever innovates... it is rejected' is cited, along with the incident of the bedouin's son (where the Prophet rejected stoning because the son was not muhsan) and the incident of Khalid ibn al-Walid (where the Prophet disassociated himself from Khalid's killing of prisoners). Finally, the athar from al-Shu'bi explicitly states the rule: rulings contrary to primary sources are rejected; but rulings based on human opinion (ra'y) are not rejected, as they fall within the realm of permissible ijtihad. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi jurisprudence to balance finality of judgments with adherence to core sources.

Key Terms
حكم الحاكم (hukm al-hakim): A judicial ruling or decision issued by a judge
قول لا دليل عليه (qawl la dalil 'alayh): A statement or ruling that has no evidence (dalil) from the Sharia sources

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when must a judge reject a previous judge's ruling?
A) When the previous judge was less knowledgeable
B) When the ruling contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma
C) When the ruling is based on personal opinion (ra'y)
D) When the ruling is more than 10 years old

Key Takeaway
A judge's ruling is binding unless it contradicts the definitive sources of Sharia or is entirely baseless.

Qada — Judiciary

Enforcing or Rejecting a Previous Judge's Verdict
Explaining two scenarios for implementing a previous judge's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios for implementing a previous judge's ruling and apply the Hanafi ruling to determine when a verdict must be enforced or rejected.

Core Idea
A judge must enforce a verdict aligned with Shariah and reject one contradicting Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma.

The authority of a judge's verdict is strong, but it is not absolute. When a subsequent judge receives a written verdict from a previous judge, he must first evaluate its conformity with the primary sources of Islamic law. This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri details two clear scenarios: enforcement when the verdict is sound, and rejection when it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma. Understanding this ruling ensures judicial consistency and fidelity to Shariah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
Read the opening sentence which divides the issue into two cases: (1) verdict not against Quran, Hadith, Ijma → enforce; (2) verdict against those sources → reject.
The term 'maktub ilayh' refers to the receiving judge.
2
Analyze the Rational Argument for Enforcement
The text provides a rational proof: since both judges possess ijtihad and a verdict has already been passed, overturning it without contravening Shariah is improper. This supports enforcement.
This argument highlights the value of judicial finality.
3
Examine the Naqli Proofs (Athar and Hadith)
For enforcement: athar of Qasim ibn Abd al-Rahman enforcing Musa ibn Anas's verdict, and Shuraih's statement not to reject prior judgments. For rejection: hadith of Aisha (innovation rejected), incident of the Bedouin's son (flogging instead of stoning), incident of Khalid ibn al-Walid (disassociation), and athar of al-Shu'bi explicitly stating the rule.
The proofs are cumulative and from reliable sources.
4
Apply the Rule to Hypothetical Situations
Test yourself: given a scenario, determine whether the receiving judge should enforce or reject based on the criteria. Consider cases where the verdict is based on ijtihad that differs from but does not contradict primary sources.
Ijtihad differences alone do not warrant rejection.

Source Text

اور قرآن ، حدیث یا اجماع کے خلاف ہو تو اس کو رد کر دے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله الا الله من احدث فی امرنا هذا ماليس فيه فهورد (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اصطلحو اعلی صلح جور فاصلح مردود ص ۳۷۱، نمبر ۲۶۹۷ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی لزوم السنته ، ج ۲، ص ۲۸۴، نمبر ۴۶۰۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شریعت میں نہ ہو تو مردود ہے۔ اس باب میں ایک دیہاتی کے بیٹے کے زنا کا واقعہ ہے۔ لوگوں نے ان کے لئے رجم کا فیصلہ کیا تو آپ نے اس کو رد فر مایا اور فرمایا کہ تمہارے بیٹے پر سو کوڑے ہیں کیونکہ وہ محسن نہیں ہے۔ (۳) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت خالد نے قیدیوں کے سلسلے میں قتل کا فیصلہ فرمایا جو شریعت کے خلاف تھا تو حضور نے اس کو رد فرمایا اور اس سے براءت ظاہر کی۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر بعث النبي قال لا اله خالدا ... فذكر نا ذلك للنبى الله الله فقال اللهم انى ابراء الیک مما صنع خالد بن الولید مرتین (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا قضی الحاکم بجور او خلاف اہل العلم فحصور در ص ۱۰۶۶، نمبر ۷۱۸۹ ) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ خلاف شریعت فیصلہ ہو تو اس کو رد کیا جائے گا اور نافذ نہیں کیا جائے گا (۴) اثر میں اس کی صراحت ہے۔ عن الشورى قال اذا قضى القاضي بخلاف كتاب الله او سنة نبي الله او شيء مجتمع عليه ، فان القاضى بعده يرده ، فان كان شيئا براى الناس لم يرده ويحمل ذلك ما تحمل (ه) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب حل برد قضاء القاضی اور جمع عن قضاء ، ج ثامن، ص ۱۳۰۲ نمبر ۱۵۲۹۸) اس اثر حاشیہ : (الف) عبد اللہ بن محرز کہتے ہیں کہ بصرہ کے قاضی موسی بن انس کا خط لیکر میں آیا اور اس کے پاس بینہ قائم کیا کہ میرا فلاں کے پاس اتنا اتنا ہے ۔ اور وہ آدمی کوفہ میں ہے۔ اور اس خط کو لیکر قاسم بن عبد الرحمن کے پاس آیا تو انہوں نے اس کو جائز قرار دیا (ب) حضرت شریح کہا کرتے تھے کہ میں پہلے لوگوں کے فیصلے کو رد نہیں کروں گا (ج) آپ نے فرمایا میرے اس معاملے میں جس نے نئی بات پیدا کی وہ رد ہے (د) آپ نے حضرت خالد و بھیجا۔ پس حضور کے سامنے خالد کے قتل کا تذکرہ کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا اے اللہ جو کچھ خالد نے کیا اس سے میں بری ہوں۔ یہ دو مرتبہ فرمایا (و) اگر قاضی کتاب اللہ کے خلاف فیصلہ کرے یا ... سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ شریعت کے خلاف ہو تو رد کر دیا جائے گا۔
In this [chapter] there are two issues. First: if the previous judge's verdict is not against the Quran, Hadith, and Ijma, then the addressed judge shall enforce it. Second: if it is against the Quran, Hadith, and Ijma, then he shall reject it. (1) If it is in accordance with Shariah, what benefit is there in rejecting? Because the previous judge also had ijtihad, and this judge also has ijtihad. And a verdict has already been made with the previous judge's ijtihad, so breaking it is not good; he should enforce it. (2) There is an athar: 'Ubaidullah ibn Mahraz narrated: I came with a letter from Musa ibn Anas, the judge of Basra, and established evidence before him that I have such-and-such with so-and-so, and he is in Kufa. I brought it to al-Qasim ibn Abd al-Rahman, and he allowed it. In this athar, al-Qasim ibn Abd al-Rahman enforced the verdict of Musa ibn Anas. (3) There is an athar from Ibn Sirin: He said, I heard Shuraih say: I do not reject a judgment that was before me. From this athar it is understood that if it is not against Shariah, one should not reject the previous judge's verdict. And if it is against the Quran, Hadith, or Ijma, he will reject it. There is a hadith from Aisha: The Messenger of Allah said, 'Whoever brings into this matter of ours something that is not of it, it is rejected.' From this hadith it is understood that whatever is not in Shariah is rejected. In this chapter is the incident of a Bedouin's son who committed zina. The people decided on stoning for him, but the Prophet rejected it and said: Your son is to be flogged one hundred lashes because he is not muhsan. (3) There is a hadith that Khalid pronounced a death sentence concerning captives which was against the Shariah, so the Prophet rejected it and disassociated himself from it. The portion of the hadith is: Ibn Umar reported: The Prophet sent Khalid... and we mentioned that to the Prophet, and he said, 'O Allah, I disassociate myself from what Khalid ibn al-Walid did,' twice. This hadith also shows that if a verdict is against Shariah, it will be rejected and not enforced. (4) There is an athar explicitly on this: from al-Shu'bi: He said, 'If a judge passes a verdict contrary to the Book of Allah, or the Sunnah of the Prophet, or something on which there is consensus, then the judge after him rejects it. But if it is a matter based on people's opinion, he does not reject it and bears its burden.' Footnote: (a) Abd Allah ibn Mahraz said: I came with a letter from Musa ibn Anas, the judge of Basra, and established evidence... (b) Shuraih used to say: I will not reject the judgment of previous people. (c) The Prophet said: Whoever brings into this matter of ours something that is not of it, it is rejected. (d) The Prophet sent Khalid... then he said: O Allah, I disassociate myself from what Khalid did, twice. (w) If a judge passes a verdict contrary to the Book of Allah... (then incomplete) From this it is also understood that if it is against Shariah, it will be rejected.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from the chapter on Qada (judicial conduct). The author first states two clear scenarios for a judge who receives a previous judge's verdict: (1) if the verdict conforms to the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, the receiving judge must enforce it; (2) if it contradicts these primary sources, he must reject it. For the first scenario, three proofs are given: first, a rational argument that since both judges have ijtihad and a verdict has been rendered, overturning it is not proper. Second, an athar from Ubaidullah ibn Mahraz where Qasim ibn Abd al-Rahman enforced the verdict of Musa ibn Anas. Third, the statement of Shuraih that he does not reject a prior judgment. For the second scenario, four proofs are provided: first, the hadith of Aisha that any innovation in religion is rejected; second, the incident of the Bedouin's son where the Prophet rejected a stoning verdict; third, the incident of Khalid ibn al-Walid where the Prophet disassociated from his verdict; fourth, the athar from al-Shu'bi explicitly stating that a judge must reject a verdict that contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, but not one based on human opinion. The footnote clarifies the Arabic sources. The overall ruling is that a judge's verdict must be in harmony with the primary sources of Shariah; otherwise it is null and void.

Key Terms
اجتہاد (ijtihād): The independent legal reasoning of a qualified jurist to derive a ruling from the primary sources.
مکتوب الیہ (maktūb ilayh): The judge who receives a written verdict from a previous judge and is asked to enforce it.
اثر (athar): A narration from a Companion or a Tabi'i, used as evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a judge do when he receives a previous judge's verdict that is contrary to the Quran?
A) He should enforce it to respect the previous judge's ijtihad.
B) He should reject it and not enforce it.
C) He should ask the previous judge for clarification.
D) He should send the case to a higher court.

Key Takeaway
A receiving judge must enforce a previous verdict if it conforms to Shariah, but must reject it if it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, regardless of the previous judge's ijtihad.

Judging an Absent Defendant: Hanafi Rule and Exceptions
Stating the rule that a judge may not rule against an absent defendant without a representative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a judge may not rule against an absent defendant, identify the exceptions to this rule, and explain the proof (dalil) and the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
A judge may not rule against an absent defendant unless a representative is present or a special cause applies equally.

This lesson explores a fundamental principle in Hanafi qada: the prohibition of passing judgment against an absent defendant. We will examine the rule, its exceptions (such as the presence of a representative or a recurring cause like nafaqah), and the strong textual proof from the hadith of Ali and the athar of Shuraih. Additionally, we will analyze the Shafi'i counterargument based on the hadith of Hind and understand why the Hanafi position remains the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
State the rule: the judge shall not pass a verdict against an absent defendant. Understand the rationale: the defendant's right to present his case is fundamental.
The matn says 'لا يقضى القاضى على غائب'.
2
List the Exceptions
Identify when judgment in absentia is allowed: (a) a representative (wakil, wasi) is present, (b) a cause that applies equally to absent and present (e.g., nafaqah claim), (c) the defendant repeatedly fails to attend despite proper summons.
The text gives the example of a wife claiming nafaqah from an absent husband.
3
Examine the Hanafi Proof
Recite the hadith of Ali: 'hear from the other as you heard from the first' which implies both sides must be heard. Also the athar of Shuraih: 'do not judge an absent person.' These are textual proofs (dalil naqli) supporting the rule.
The hadith is from Abu Dawood and Tirmidhi.
4
Understand the Shafi'i Objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that judging in absentia is permissible to prevent loss of the plaintiff's right, citing the hadith of Hind where the Prophet allowed her to take maintenance from Abu Sufyan despite his absence.
The Shafi'i view prioritizes avoiding loss of the plaintiff's right.
5
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi school responds that the hadith of Hind is specific to the case of darurah (hardship) and does not establish a general rule. The exceptions in the Hanafi view are limited and defined.
Thus the Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that judgment against an absent defendant is not allowed without a representative or exceptional cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۲۲] (۳۵) ولا يقضى القاضى على غائب الا ان يحضر من يقوم مقامه.
پہلے تفصیل گزرچکی ہے کہ مدعی علیہ غائب ہو تو اس پر فیصلہ نہ کیا جائے۔ ہاں ! اس کا کوئی قائم مقام موجود ہو، مثلا اس کا وکیل موجود ہویا وصی موجود ہو یا ایسا سبب ہو جو غائب پر بھی لگتا ہو اور حاضر پر بھی لگتا ہو یا بار بار خبر دینے کے باوجود حاضر نہ ہوتا ہو، مثلا عورت غائب شوہر پر نفقہ کا دعوی کر رہی ہو اور شوہر زمانے سے غائب ہو اور عورت کے لئے نفقے کی کوئی صورت نہ ہو تو غائب پر فیصلہ کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ عن علی ... فقال ان الله سیهدی قلبک ویثبت لسانک فاذا جلس بین یدیک الخصمان فلا تقضين حتى تسمع من الآخر كما سمعت من الاول فانه احرى ان يتبين لك القضاء (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب كيف القضاء، ص ۱۴۸، نمبر ۳۵۸۲) ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی القاضی لا یقضی بین الخصمین حتی یسمع كلامهما ص ۲۴۸، نمبر ۱۳۳۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کی بات بھی سنوتب فیصلہ کرو۔ اور یہ اسی وقت ہوسکتا ہے جب مدعی علیہ حاضر ہو یا اس کا قائم مقام حاضر ہو اور اپنی بات سنا سکے (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ مسمعت شريحا يقول لا يقضى على غائب (ب) (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب لا یقضی علی غائب، ج : ثامن ص ۱۳۰۴، نمبر ۱۵۳۰۶) فانده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ مدعی علیہ مجلس قضا سے غائب ہو یا شہر سے غائب ہو یا شہر میں چھپ گیا ہو تو غا ئب مدعی علیہ پر فیصلہ کیا جاسکتا
اگر ایسا نہ کریں تو مدعی کا حق ضائع ہوگا اور مدعی علیہ خواہ مخواہ ٹال مٹول کرتا رہے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة ان هندا قالت للنبي الله ان ابا سفيان رجل شحيح واحتاج ان آخذ من ماله ، قال له خذی مایکفیک وولدک بالمعروف (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب القضاء علی الغائب، ص ۱۰۶۴، نمبر ۷۱۸۰ مسلم شریف ، باب قضیہ ہند ، ج ۲، ص ۷۵ نمبر ۱۷۱۴) اس حدیث میں حضرت سفیان حاضر نہیں تھے پھر بھی ان کے مال سے نفقہ لینے کا فیصلہ کیا گیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ غائب پر فیصلہ کیا جاسکتا ہے۔
[2922] (35) The judge shall not pass a verdict against an absent person unless someone representing him is present. The detail has already passed: if the defendant is absent, a verdict shall not be passed against him. Yes, if there is a representative of his present, e.g., his agent or guardian is present, or there is a cause that applies both to the absent and the present, or if despite repeated summons he does not attend, e.g., a woman claims maintenance from an absentee husband who has been absent for a long time and there is no way for the woman to get maintenance, then a verdict can be passed against the absent. A hadith has already passed: from Ali... He said: 'Indeed Allah will guide your heart and make your tongue firm. When the two litigants sit before you, do not pronounce judgment until you hear from the other as you heard from the first, for that is more likely to make the judgment clear to you.' In this hadith, the statement of the defendant must also be heard, and that is only possible when the defendant is present or his representative is present and can state his case. (3) There is an athar: I heard Shuraih say: 'Do not pass a judgment against an absent person.' So Imam Shafi'i says: If the defendant is absent from the court session, or absent from the city, or has hidden himself in the city, then a verdict can be passed against the absent defendant. If that is not done, the plaintiff's right will be lost and the defendant will keep evading. (2) There is a hadith from Aisha: Hind said to the Prophet: 'Abu Sufyan is a miserly man, and I need to take from his wealth.' He said: 'Take what suffices you and your child in a reasonable manner.' In this hadith, Abu Sufyan was not present, yet a verdict was passed to take maintenance from his wealth, so it shows that a verdict can be passed against an absent person.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage, a ruling with proof, addresses the permissibility of judging an absent defendant. The Hanafi position, based on the matn, is that a judge should not pass a verdict against an absent person unless that person has a representative (wakil, wasi) present. Exceptions include cases where a recurring cause applies equally to the absent and present, or when the defendant repeatedly fails to appear despite proper notification. The example of a woman claiming nafaqah from an absent husband is given. The hadith of Ali (ra) stresses hearing both sides, implying the defendant or his representative must be present. The athar of Shuraih affirms 'no judgment against an absent.' Imam Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that judgment in absentia is permissible to prevent loss of the plaintiff's right, citing the hadith of Hind where Abu Sufyan was absent but judgment was made. The Hanafi response interprets that hadith as specific to the case of hardship, not a general rule. The mufta bihi position is the Hanafi one: judgment against an absent defendant is not allowed without a representative, except in specific exceptional cases.

Key Terms
غائب (ghā’ib): A defendant who is not present in the court session, either physically absent from the city or hiding.
قائم مقام (qā’im maqām): A representative such as a wakil (agent) or wasi (guardian) who can speak on behalf of the absent defendant.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter, which a wife is entitled to from her husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, when can a judge pass a verdict against an absent defendant?
A) Only if the defendant is hiding within the city.
B) Only if a representative of the defendant is present in court.
C) Whenever the plaintiff demands it to prevent loss of his right.
D) Never under any circumstances.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits judgment against an absent defendant unless a representative is present or a specific exception like nafaqah applies, ensuring both parties have the opportunity to be heard.

Judgment on an Absent Defendant
States the rule and exceptions for judging absent parties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on judgment against an absent defendant and identify the exceptions where it is permissible, including when a representative is present or in cases of necessity such as maintenance.

Core Idea
Judgment against an absent defendant is prohibited unless a representative is present or necessity demands it.

This passage addresses a critical aspect of judicial procedure in Hanafi fiqh: when can a judge pass judgment against a defendant who is not present? The default rule is that it is not allowed, but the text enumerates important exceptions. Understanding these exceptions is essential for protecting plaintiffs' rights while upholding the principle of hearing both sides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling and exceptions
Read the initial statement: 'The judge shall not pass judgment on an absent person' — this is the default. Then note the exception: 'unless someone who stands in his place is present.' Identify the specific scenarios listed: representative (agent, executor), a cause that applies equally, repeated absence despite notice, and the maintenance example.
The maintenance case is a key example of necessity overriding the general prohibition.
2
Examine the primary proof (hadith of Ali)
Analyze the hadith in which the Prophet instructs Ali to hear both parties before judging. Determine how the Hanafi school uses this to require the presence of the defendant or his representative.
The phrase 'hear from the other' implies either the actual defendant or someone speaking for him.
3
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Read the section where Imam Shafi'i's position is presented: he allows judgment on an absent defendant more broadly to prevent loss of the plaintiff's right. Contrast this with the Hanafi restriction.
The hadith of Hind is used by Shafi'i as proof, but Hanafis interpret it as a case of necessity.
4
Apply the rule to practical scenarios
Test the rule with examples: a woman suing for maintenance from an absent husband, a creditor against an absent debtor with a present agent, etc. Identify which conditions are met.
The presence of a qa'im maqam is the most common permissible scenario.

آپ نے فرمایا اتنا لو جتنا مناسب انداز میں تمہیں اور تمہاری اولاد کے لئے کافی ہو۔
And the judge shall not pass judgment on an absent person unless someone who stands in his place is present. From this it is also understood that if it is against the Sharia, it will be rejected. (2922) (35) The judge shall not pass judgment on an absent person except if someone representing him is present. The detail has passed before: if the defendant is absent, judgment shall not be passed against him. Yes, if his representative is present, for example, his agent is present, or his executor is present, or there is a cause that applies to the absent and also applies to the present, or despite repeated notices he does not appear, for example, a woman claims maintenance from an absent husband, and the husband has been absent for a long time, and there is no way for the woman to obtain maintenance, then judgment can be passed against the absent. A hadith has passed: From Ali... he said: 'Indeed Allah will guide your heart and make firm your tongue. When the two litigants sit before you, do not judge until you hear from the other as you heard from the first, for it is more likely that the judgment will become clear to you.' (A) (Abu Dawud, Bab Kayf al-Qada, p. 148, no. 3582; Tirmidhi, Bab Ma Ja'a fi al-Qadi la Yaqdi bayn al-Khasmayn hatta Yasma'a Kalamahuma, p. 248, no. 1331). In this hadith, hear the statement of the defendant as well before judging. And this is only possible when the defendant is present or his representative is present and can present his case. (3) There is an athar: I heard Shuraih say: 'Do not judge against an absent person.' (B) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab La Yaqdi 'ala Gha'ib, vol. 8, p. 1304, no. 15306). Then Imam Shafi'i says: If the defendant is absent from the court session, or absent from the city, or has hidden in the city, then judgment can be passed against the absent defendant. If this is not done, the plaintiff's right will be lost, and the defendant will keep delaying unnecessarily. (2) There is a hadith: From Aisha that Hind said to the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Abu Sufyan is a miserly man, and I need to take from his wealth.' He said: 'Take what suffices you and your child in a reasonable manner.' (C) (Bukhari, Bab al-Qada' 'ala al-Gha'ib, p. 1064, no. 7180; Muslim, Bab Qadiyyat Hind, vol. 2, p. 75, no. 1714). In this hadith, Abu Sufyan was not present, yet judgment was given to take maintenance from his wealth. From this it is understood that judgment can be passed against an absent person. Footnote: (continued from previous page) If it is against the Sunnah of the Messenger or against any consensus, then the subsequent judge will reject it. And if it is based on people's opinion, he will not reject it but will continue what he said, because it is not against the Sharia. (A) You said to Ali: 'Allah will guide your heart and make your tongue firm. So when the two parties sit before you, do not judge until you hear the other's statement.' Therefore it is more appropriate that the judgment become clear to you. (B) Shuraih used to say: Do not judge against an absent person. (C) Hind said to the Prophet: 'Abu Sufyan is a miser, and I need to take his wealth?' He said: 'Take as much as is sufficient for you and your children in a reasonable manner.'
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the permissibility of passing judgment against an absent defendant. The core rule, stated in the matn, is that a judge should not pass judgment on an absent person unless someone representing him is present. The commentary expands on this by listing several exceptions: if the absent person has a representative present (agent, executor), if there is a cause that applies equally to absent and present (e.g., a recurring obligation), or if the defendant repeatedly fails to appear despite notification. A key example given is a woman claiming maintenance from an absent husband: if the husband is long absent and there is no other recourse, judgment may be passed. The author then provides several proofs. First, a hadith from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi in which the Prophet instructs Ali to hear both parties before judging, implying that both litigants (or their representatives) must be heard. Second, an athar from Shuraih stating the general prohibition. Then the commentary notes that Imam Shafi'i allows judgment against an absent defendant if he is absent from the session, the city, or is hiding, to prevent the plaintiff's right from being lost. This is supported by the hadith of Hind, where the Prophet allowed her to take from Abu Sufyan's wealth despite his absence. The footnote adds that a later judge can only reject a previous judgment if it contradicts the Sharia; if based on valid opinion, it stands. The Hanafi position, as derived from these sources, allows judgment against an absent defendant under specific conditions, balancing the need to protect the plaintiff's right with the principle of hearing both sides.

Key Terms
غائب (gha'ib): A defendant who is not present in the court or city at the time of judgment.
قضاء (qada'): Judicial decision or verdict passed by a judge.
قائم مقام (qa'im maqam): Representative who stands in the place of the absent party, such as an agent (wakil), executor (wasi), or guardian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits judgment against an absent defendant only when a representative is present or in specific exigencies, balancing the principle of hearing both sides with preventing loss of rights.

Permissibility of Arbitration (Tahkim) with Mutual Consent
States ruling on mutual arbitration with judge-like qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for valid Hanafi arbitration (tahkim) and cite the hadith of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh as evidence.

Core Idea
Arbitration is valid when both parties consent and the arbitrator has a judge's qualifications.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on arbitration (tahkim). Arbitration is a common alternative dispute resolution mechanism where litigants appoint a third party to settle their case. The Hanafi school permits it under specific conditions, relying on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the hadith of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh. We will break down the ruling, its conditions, and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tahkim: two litigants appointing a third person to judge their dispute. The ruling is ja'iz (permissible) if conditions are met.
The passage states 'jaza' (permissible) explicitly.
2
List the conditions for validity
Two conditions: (1) both parties must consent to the arbitrator; (2) the arbitrator must possess the qualities of a judge (Muslim, free, sane, adult, not convicted of qadhf, just).
The arbitrator is not a state-appointed judge, so his authority derives solely from mutual consent.
3
Examine the dalil (proof)
The primary evidence is the hadith of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, where the Prophet accepted Sa'd's arbitration over Banu Qurayza. This shows the permissibility of tahkim by mutual consent.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the point)
The Prophet explicitly referred the judgment to Sa'd and accepted the parties' consent to his arbitration, establishing that mutually agreed arbitration is legitimate.
The Hanafi school uses prophetic action (fi'l) as a source of law.

واذا حكم رجلان رجلا بينهما ورضيا بحكمه جاز اذا كان بصفة الحاكم

کتاب آداب القاضی (36) اگر دو آدمیوں نے ایک آدمی کو پنچ بنایا تا کہ دونوں کے درمیان فیصلہ کرے اور دونوں اس کے فیصلے پر راضی ہوں تو جائز ہے جبکہ وہ حاکم کی صفت پر ہو۔ مدگی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں نے قاضی کے بجائے کسی آدمی کو درمیان میں حکم اور فیصل چن لئے ، اور حکم میں وہ صفات ہیں جو قاضی میں ہوا کرتے ہیں۔ مثلا مسلمان ہے، آزاد ہے، عاقل اور بالغ ہے، محدود فی القذف نہیں ہے اور عادل ہے تو ایسے آدمی کو حکم بنانا درست ہے۔ اور وہ جو فیصلہ کر دے اس کو مان لینا چاہئے۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ بنو قریظہ کے یہود نے حضور کے بجائے حضرت سعد بن معاد کو حکم بنایا اور انہوں نے جو فیصلہ فرمایا وہ دونوں فریقوں کو مانا پڑا ۔ یہی حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت اصيب سعد يوم الخندق ... فاشار الى بني قريظة فاتاهم رسول الله فنزلوا على حكمه فرد الحكم الى سعد، قال فانى احكم فيهم الخ (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب مرجع النبی و من الاحزاب و مخرجہ الی بنی قریظة ومحاصرته اياهم، کتاب المغازی، ص۵۹۰، نمبر ۴۱۲۲ / مسلم شریف، باب جواز قتال من نقض العهد و جواز انزال اہل الحسن علی حکم حاکم عدل اہل الحکم میں ۹۵ نمبر ۱۷۶۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپس میں کسی کو پیچ بنانا جائز ہے۔ البتہ حکم بنانے کے لئے دو شرطیں ہیں۔ ایک تو یہ کہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں حکم بنا ئیں تب فیصلہ کر سکیں گے، کیونکہ یہ امیر کی جانب سے قاضی نہیں ہے کہ دونوں پر قضاء کا اختیار رکھتا ہو۔ اس لئے دونوں کے ماننے سے ہوگا، اور دونوں میں سے ایک کے نہ ماننے سے حکم نہیں بن سکے گا۔ دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ حکم میں قاضی کی صفت ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ گواہوں سے گواہی لیکر فیصلہ کریں گے تو گواہوں میں جو صفتیں ہوں کم از کم پنچ میں بھی وہ صفتیں ہوں تا کہ وہ فیصلہ کر سکے۔
And if two men appoint a man as arbitrator between them and they are satisfied with his judgment, it is permissible if he is of the description of a judge. Book of Etiquette of the Judge: (36) If two persons make one person an arbitrator so that he decides between them, and both are pleased with his decision, it is permissible, provided he has the quality of a judge. The plaintiff and defendant choose a person instead of a judge for judgment and decision, and the arbitrator must have the qualities that a judge has: e.g., Muslim, free, sane, adult, not convicted of slander, and just; then appointing such a person as arbitrator is valid. And whatever decision he gives must be accepted. There is a hadith that the Jews of Banu Qurayza made Sa'd ibn Mu'adh arbitrator instead of the Prophet, and they had to accept his decision. The hadith is: 'A'ishah said: Sa'd was struck on the day of the trench... then he pointed towards Banu Qurayza, and the Messenger of Allah came to them, and they agreed to his judgment, and he referred the judgment to Sa'd. He said: I judge among them...' (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith it is known that appointing someone as arbitrator among oneself is permissible. However, there are two conditions for making an arbitrator: first, both the plaintiff and defendant must make him arbitrator then he can decide, because he is not a judge appointed by the ruler who has authority over both; so it will be only with both's consent, and if one does not agree, he cannot be made arbitrator. Second, the arbitrator must have the quality of a judge, because he will take testimony from witnesses and decide, so the qualities that are in witnesses must at least be in the arbitrator so that he can decide.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on tahkim (arbitration). It states that if two litigants mutually agree to appoint a third person as arbitrator to settle their dispute, it is valid provided that person possesses the qualifications of a judge. The commentary elaborates that the arbitrator must be Muslim, free, sane, adult, not convicted of qadhf (false accusation of adultery), and just. The proof cited is the well-known hadith of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepted the arbitration of Sa'd regarding the Banu Qurayza. This establishes the legitimacy of tahkim. Two conditions are emphasized: (1) both parties must consent to the arbitration, since the arbitrator is not a state-appointed judge with inherent authority; (2) the arbitrator must have the same qualities as a judge, as he will be hearing testimony and adjudicating.

Key Terms
تحكيم (tahkim): Arbitration: appointing a third party to settle a dispute by mutual consent.
محكم (muhakkam): The arbitrator appointed by the litigants.
بصفة الحاكم (bi-sifat al-hakim): Possessing the attributes of a judge: Muslim, free, sane, adult, not convicted of slander, just.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The hadith of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh regarding Banu Qurayza

D) Analogy (Qiyas) to a ruler's appointment

Key Takeaway
Arbitration (tahkim) in the Hanafi school is valid when both parties mutually consent and the arbitrator has the qualifications of a judge, as evidenced by the prophetic practice.

Ineligibility of Certain Persons for Arbitration
Ruling on ineligibility of six categories for arbitration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six categories of persons who cannot be appointed as arbitrators in Hanafi law and explain the evidence for each category.

Core Idea
Six categories lack judge qualifications; appointing them as arbitrators is prohibited.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri lists six types of individuals who are ineligible to serve as arbitrators because they lack the necessary attributes of a judge. Each category is supported by textual proof (Quran, athar) or reasoning. Understanding these disqualifications clarifies the prerequisites for valid arbitration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Six Categories
List the six types of persons prohibited from being arbitrators: disbeliever, slave, dhimmi, one lashed for qadhf, fasiq, and child.
2
Identify the Deficiency
For each category, determine which qualification of a judge is missing: e.g., kafir lacks authority over a Muslim, slave lacks authority over himself, etc.
3
Locate the Proof
Find the evidence cited for each category: Quran 4:141 for kafir, athar on testimony for slave and child, Quran 24:4 for one lashed for qadhf, and lack of 'adalah for fasiq.
4
Note the Exception for Fasiq
Understand that although appointing a fasiq is prohibited, if a fasiq is actually appointed and issues a judgment, it is enforced due to practical necessity.
5
Derive the Principle
Conclude that arbitrators must possess the same qualifications as judges: freedom, sanity, probity, and authority over the disputants.

Source Text

[۲۹۲۴] (۳۷) ولا يجوز تحكيم الكافر والعبد والذمي والمحدود في القذف والفاسق والصبي

حکم پنچ بنانے کا بیان (37) اور نہیں جائز ہے کا فر کو اور غلام کو اور زمی کو اور تہمت میں حد لگے ہوئے کو اور فاسق کو اور بچے کو پہنچ بنانا۔ ان چھ قسم کے آدمیوں کو حکم بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان میں قاضی کی صفت پورے طور پر نہیں پائی جاتی ،مثلا کافر کے بارے میں آیت ہے کہ اس کو مسلمان پر اختیار نہیں۔ آیت یہ ہے۔ ولن يجعل الله للكافرين على المومنين سبيلا (ب) ( آیت ۱۴۱، سورۃ النساء ) (۲) اثر میں ہے کہ مسلمان کے خلاف غیر مسلم کی شہادت مقبول نہیں تو اس کی قضا کیسے مقبول ہوگی۔ عن ابراهيم عن شريح قال: لا تجوز شهادة اليهودى والنصراني الا في سفر، ولا تجوز الا على وصية (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی هیبتة ، ۳۵۵ ما تجوز فیہ شہادۃ الیہودی والنصرانی، ج رابع ، حاشیه : (الف) حضرت سعد گو غزوہ خندق میں تیر لگا ۔ پس انہوں نے بنی قریظہ کی طرف اشارہ کیا۔ پس وہ لوگ حضور کے پاس آئے اور حضرت سعد کے فیصلے پر اتفاق کیا۔ حضرت سعد نے فرمایا میں بنو قریضہ کے لئے اللہ کا فیصلہ کروں گا (ب) اللہ نے کافر کا مومن پر کوئی راستہ نہیں بنایا (ج) یہودی اور (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )

 الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع) ۱۹۹ كتاب آداب القاضي والفاسق والصبي [۲۹۲۵] (۳۸) ولكل واحد من المُحكّمين ان يرجع مالم يحكم عليهما.

ص ۴۹۵، نمبر ۲۲۴۳۹ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب شہادۃ اہل الکفر علی اہل الاسلام، ج ثامن، ص ۱۳۶۰، نمبر ۱۵۵۳۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہی بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ ذمی بھی اسی میں داخل ہے کہ اس کو حکم بنانا بھی جائز نہیں۔ غلام کو حکم بنانا اس لئے صحیح نہیں ہے کہ اس کو اپنے اوپر اختیار نہیں ہے تو دوسرے پر فیصلے کا اختیار کیسے ملے گا (۲) اس کو تو گواہی دینے کی بھی اجازت نہیں ہے فیصلہ کیسے کرے گا۔ اثر میں ہے۔ روی عن على والحسن والنخعى والزهري ومجاهد وعطاء لا تجوز شهادة العبيد (الف) (سن اليقي ، باب من رو شهادة العبيد ومن قبلها ، ج عاشر ص۲۷۲، نمبر ۲۰۶۰۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ غلام کی گواہی درست نہیں۔ اس لئے اس کو حکم بنانا بھی درست نہیں ہے۔ محدود في القذف کو بھی حکم بنانا درست نہیں ہے۔ آیت میں ہے۔ ولا تقبلوا لهم شهادة ابدا واولئك هم الفاسقون (ب) ( آیت ۴ ، سورۃ النور ۲۴) اس کی جب گواہی مقبول نہیں تو یہ گواہ سے گواہی لیکر فیصلہ کیسے کرے گا۔ فاسق کو حکم بنانا بھی اچھا نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ عادل نہیں ہے۔ تاہم اگر فاسق کو حکم بنا دیا تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ حجاج بن یوسف فاسق تھا پھر بھی وہ حکم تھا اور اس کے فیصلے نافذ ہوتے تھے۔ اس لئے فاسق کو قاضی یا حکم بنادیا اور اس نے فیصلہ کر دیا تو نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ بچے اور مجنون کو تو عقل ہی نہیں ہے ان کو حکم کیسے بنائے گا۔ اس کی تو گواہی بھی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ ارسل الى ابن عباس . يسأله عن شهادة الصبيان فقال: لا ارى ان تجوز شهادتهم (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة الصبیان، ج ثامن ، ص ۱۳۴۲۸ نمبر ۱۵۴۹۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بچے کی گواہی مقبول نہیں تو اس کو حکم بنانا کیسے درست ہوگا۔
It is not permissible to appoint as arbitrator: the disbeliever, the slave, the dhimmi, the one who has been lashed for qadhf (false accusation), the fasiq (sinner), and the child. Statement on arbitration: (37) It is not permissible to make an arbitrator: a disbeliever, a slave, a dhimmi, one who has been lashed for false accusation, a fasiq, and a child. Appointing these six types of persons as arbitrators is not correct because they do not fully possess the quality of a judge. For example, regarding the disbeliever, there is the verse: 'And Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers' (Surah an-Nisa 4:141). Also, there is an athar: from Ibrahim from Shurayh: 'The testimony of a Jew or Christian is not permissible except in travel, and not permissible except regarding a will' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). This shows that testimony is not permissible; the dhimmi is included in this, so appointing him as arbitrator is not permissible. Appointing a slave as arbitrator is not correct because he does not have authority over himself, so how can he have authority to decide over others? Also, he is not allowed to give testimony. There is an athar: from Ali, Hasan, Nakha'i, Zuhri, Mujahid, and Ata: 'The testimony of slaves is not permissible' (Sunan al-Kubra). So appointing him as arbitrator is not correct. Appointing one lashed for qadhf is not correct. The verse says: 'And never accept their testimony, and those are the defiantly disobedient' (Surah an-Nur 24:4). Since his testimony is not accepted, how can he take testimony from witnesses and decide? Appointing a fasiq as arbitrator is not good because he is not just. However, if a fasiq is appointed as arbitrator and he gives a decision, it will be enforced. Hajjaj ibn Yusuf was a fasiq, yet he was a governor and his decisions were enforced. Therefore, if a fasiq is made a judge or arbitrator and he decides, it will be effective. As for a child or an insane person, they have no intellect; how can they be appointed? Their testimony is not accepted. There is an athar: 'The Prophet was asked about the testimony of children via Ibn Abbas, and he said: I do not think their testimony is permissible' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq). So if a child's testimony is not accepted, how can appointing him as arbitrator be correct?
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that six categories of people cannot be appointed as arbitrators because they lack the full qualifications of a judge. The text uses multiple proofs: for the kafir, Quran 4:141 which denies authority of disbelievers over believers; for the slave and the child, lack of capacity for testimony is cited; for the one convicted of qadhf, Quran 24:4 prohibits accepting his testimony; for the fasiq, lack of justice is given, though an exception is noted that if a fasiq is actually appointed and pronounces a judgment, it is still executed as a matter of authority. The dhimmi (non-Muslim subject) is included with the kafir based on the principle that their testimony is not accepted except in limited cases. The commentary also cites athar (reports from early authorities) to support each point.

Key Terms
محدود في القذف (muhaddud fi al-qadhf): One who has been legally lashed for committing qadhf (false accusation of adultery or illegitimacy).
فاسق (fasiq): A person who openly commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking 'adalah (moral probity).
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the text consider a slave ineligible for arbitration?
A) Because slaves lack intellectual capacity
B) Because slaves cannot give testimony, so they cannot judge based on testimony
C) Because slaves are not Muslim
D) Because slaves have no right to property

Key Takeaway
Appointing a person who lacks judicial qualifications (kafir, slave, dhimmi, lashed for qadhf, fasiq, child) as an arbitrator is prohibited, though a fasiq's judgment is enforceable if already given.
