Division When Both Partners Are Harmed
Ruling on division when both partners are harmed by the division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on division when both partners are harmed and apply the condition of mutual consent in such cases.

Core Idea
Division that harms both is only valid by mutual consent – no one may be forced to suffer loss.

This passage addresses a situation where dividing jointly owned property would cause harm to both owners, such as a mill that becomes unusable when split. The Hanafi school rules that in such a case, the qadi cannot enforce division unless both parties willingly consent. The proof is drawn from the Prophetic principle of prohibiting harm and a mursal hadith on inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The author presents the example of a mill jointly owned by two people. After division, neither can benefit – both are harmed.
The harm is mutual and makes the divided parts valueless.
2
State the ruling
Division is not made except with the mutual consent of both partners. If only one consents, division does not take place.
The ruling is based on the principle of preventing harm.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof includes the general rule 'la darar wa la dirar' and a mursal hadith: 'لا تعضية على اهل الميراث الا ما حمل القسم' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi).
Taʿḍiyah means harmful subdivision.
4
Explain the condition
The key condition is mutual consent. Without it, the qadi must not order division even if both are harmed.
Consent removes the prohibition arising from harm.
5
Apply the ruling
This ruling applies to any jointly owned property where division would harm all owners. Only with full consent is division valid.
The same rule applies to heirs and other joint owners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۴۵] (۱۴) اور اگر دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کو نقصان ہو تو اس کو تقسیم نہ کرے مگر دونوں کی رضامندی سے۔ کوئی ایسی چیز ہے جس کو تقسیم کرنے کے بعد دونوں کو نقصان ہوگا تو دونوں راضی ہوں تو تقسیم کر دے۔ اور ایک حصہ دار کہے اور دوسرا نہ کہے تو تقسیم نہ کرے۔ مثلا ایک چکی دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے۔ اس کو تقسیم کرنے کے بعد کوئی بھی فائدہ نہیں اٹھا سکے گا، دونوں کو نقصان ہو گا۔ اس لئے دونوں اس نقصان پر راضی ہوں تو تقسیم کر دی جائے گی۔ یہاں دونوں کو نقصان ہے اس لئے دونوں کی رضامندی سے تقسیم کر دیں گے۔ قاعدہ وہی ہے لا ضرر ولا ضرار (۲) حدیث مرسل میں ہے۔ عن محمد بن ابی بکر یعنی ابن حزم عن ابيه عن النبي الله قال لا تعضية على اهل الميراث الا ما حمل القسم ، يقول لا يبعض على الوارث ... قال ابو عبيد قوله لا تعضية في ميراث يعنى ان يموت الميت ويدع شيئا ان قسم بين ورثته اذا اراد بعضهم القسمة كان في ذلك ضرر عليه او على بعضهم يقول فلا يقسم والتعضية التفريق (ب) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب مالا تحتمل القسمة ، ج عاشر ص ۲۲۵، نمبر ۲۰۴۴۷/۲۰۴۴۶) اس حدیث مرسل میں ہے کہ اگر تقسیم سے نقصان ہوتا ہو تو دونوں کی رضامندی کے بغیر تقسیم نہ کرے۔
[2945] (14) And if both of them are harmed, then do not divide except with the consent of both. Something that, after division, will cause harm to both, then if both agree, divide. And if one partner says and the other does not, then do not divide. For example, a mill jointly owned by two people. After dividing it, neither can benefit; both will be harmed. So if both agree to this harm, then division will be made. Here both are harmed, so we will divide only with the consent of both. The principle is the same: 'no harm and no reciprocating harm.' (2) A mursal hadith: from Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, meaning Ibn Hazm, from his father, from the Prophet ﷺ: 'There is no subdivision (taʿḍiyah) for the heirs except what division carries.' He says: do not subdivide for the heir... Abu Ubayd said: his saying 'no subdivision in inheritance' means that if a person dies and leaves something, and if it is divided among his heirs, and some of them want division, and there is harm in that for him or for some of them, he says: do not divide. And taʿḍiyah means division. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab ma la tahtamilu al-qasmah, vol. 10, p. 225, no. 20447/20446). In this mursal hadith, it is that if division causes harm, then do not divide without the consent of both.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, addressing the case where both partners would be harmed by division. The author uses the example of a mill (chakki) owned jointly. If divided, each part would be too small to function, so both lose. In such a case, division is only permitted with the mutual consent of both partners. If one partner requests but the other does not agree, the qadi must not enforce division. The proof is the hadith 'la darar wa la dirar' and a mursal hadith from Bayhaqi which states that there is no taʿḍiyah (subdivision) in inheritance if it causes harm. Taʿḍiyah refers to splitting property into portions that render it useless. This reinforces the principle that the qadi must protect against harm and cannot force a division that harms both parties without their consent. The ruling is a straightforward application of the harm principle.

Key Terms
تعضية (taʿḍiyah): Subdivision of joint property into portions that are detrimental, causing harm to the owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When both partners are harmed by division, when can the qadi enforce division?
A) At the request of one partner
B) Only if both partners consent
C) Never
D) At the request of a third party

Key Takeaway
Division that harms all joint owners is only valid with the mutual consent of everyone; otherwise the qadi must not enforce it.

Compulsory Division of Homogeneous Goods
Ruling on compulsory division of identical goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compulsory division of homogenous goods and identify the condition that permits enforcement.

Core Idea
Qadi may enforce division of identical goods because no harm results from equal partition.

Imagine two partners own a single heap of wheat. One wants to divide it, the other refuses. Can the qadi force a division? The Hanafi school says yes, but only if the goods are of a single type and can be divided equally without any qualitative difference. This lesson examines the ruling and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of goods
Determine if the co-owned property consists of a single type (homogeneous) or multiple types (heterogeneous). In the passage, wheat is given as a single type.
Homogeneous goods are fungible and identical in kind.
2
Apply the rule for homogeneous goods
For goods of the same type, the qadi can enforce division without the consent of all partners. This is because equal division by weight or measure causes no harm to any partner.
The condition is that the division must be exactly equal and the goods must be identical.
3
Understand the condition: no harm
The permissibility of compulsory division hinges on the absence of harm. When goods are identical and divided equally by the same measure, no one receives a lesser share.
If division would cause harm (e.g., one partner gets a poorer quality part), consent is required.
4
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Some other schools may require consent even for homogeneous goods. In the Hanafi view, the potential harm is negligible, so the qadi may proceed.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the broader tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۴۶] (۱۵) تقسیم کر دے سامان جبکہ ایک ہی قسم کا ہو، اور دو جنسوں کو تقسیم نہ کرے بعض کو بعض میں مگر دونوں کی رضا مندی سے۔ اگر سامان ایک ہی قسم کا ہو مثلا چالیس کیلو گیہوں ہو تو بغیر دونوں کی رضامندی کے بھی تقسیم کردے۔ اور دونوں حصہ داروں کو بیس بیس کیلو گیہوں دیدے۔ تمام گیہوں ہی ہیں اور ایک ہی جنس کا سامان ہے، اور گیہوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ اور وزن میں دونوں کو برابر یعنی بیس بیس کیلو دیا گیا ہے اس لئے کسی کو کچھ نقصان نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے ایک راضی نہ بھی ہو تو قاضی جبر اتقسیم کر دے۔ لیکن اگر دو جنس کے سامان ہوں مثلا دس کپڑے ہیں اور چالیس کیلو گیہوں ہے۔ اب بغیر دونوں کی رضامندی کے ایک حصے دار کو کپڑے اور دوسرے کو گیہوں نہیں دے سکتے، کیونکہ دونوں جنس مختلف ہیں۔ اس صورت میں دونوں کی رضامندی ضروری ہے۔
[2946] (15) He divides goods when they are of the same type, and he should not divide two different types into parts without the consent of both. If the goods are of the same type, for example forty kilos of wheat, then he divides even without the consent of both. He gives each of the two partners twenty kilos of wheat. All is wheat, it is a single type of goods, and there is no difference in the wheat. And in weight, both are given equally, i.e., twenty kilos each, so no one will suffer any harm. Therefore, even if one is not pleased, the qadi enforces division. But if the goods are of two types, for example ten cloths and forty kilos of wheat, then without the consent of both, he cannot give cloths to one and wheat to the other, because the two types are different. In that case, the consent of both is necessary.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the compulsory division of fungible goods (mithliyyat). The author explains that if the property consists of a single type of good, such as wheat, the qadi can enforce division even against the will of a partner. This is because the goods are identical and can be divided equally by weight or measure without any qualitative difference, thus no harm occurs. However, if the property consists of two different types of goods, such as cloth and wheat, the qadi cannot enforce a division that gives one partner cloth and the other wheat without their mutual consent. This is because the types are distinct and valuation might differ, so harm or inequality could result. The ruling is based on the principle that compulsory partition (qismah jabriyyah) is only allowed when no harm results from the division. When the goods are of the same type and equal division is straightforward, there is no harm; when types differ, consent is required.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Type or category of goods; e.g., wheat is one jins, cloth is another.
قسمت جبری (qismah jabriyyah): Compulsory partition enforced by the qadi without the consent of all co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when can a qadi enforce division of co-owned goods without consent?
A) Only when the goods are of different types
B) Only when the goods are of the same type and can be divided equally without harm
C) Whenever any partner requests division
D) Never, consent is always required

Key Takeaway
Compulsory division of co-owned goods is permitted only when the goods are homogeneous and equal division causes no harm.

Consensual Division of Heterogeneous Goods
Ruling on consensual division of different types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when consent is required for division of co-owned goods and apply the ruling to multi-type property.

Core Idea
When goods are of different types, the qadi cannot enforce division without the consent of all partners.

What happens if two partners own a mix of cloth and wheat? The Hanafi ruling is clear: the qadi cannot force a division that gives one partner cloth and the other wheat unless both agree. This lesson explores the rationale behind requiring consent for heterogeneous goods and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the presence of multiple types
Check if the co-owned property includes goods of different categories (e.g., cloth and wheat). These are heterogeneous.
Even if each type is homogeneous individually, the mix as a whole is heterogeneous.
2
Apply the consent requirement
The qadi cannot partition heterogeneous goods by giving one type to one partner and another type to the other without mutual consent. This is because the types have different values and uses, so unequal harm would likely occur.
The ruling protects partners from being forced into an unequal exchange.
3
Understand the rationale: potential harm
Unlike identical goods where equal division is straightforward, different types cannot be divided equally without evaluating their relative values. Forcing such a division could cause significant harm to one party.
Consent ensures that each partner accepts the valuation or exchange.
4
Contrast with homogeneous goods ruling
Recall that for a single type, the qadi can force division. The key difference is the presence or absence of potential harm due to type disparity.
This contrast highlights the Hanafi principle of preventing harm (darar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[2946] (15) He divides goods when they are of the same type, and he should not divide two different types into parts without the consent of both. If the goods are of the same type, for example forty kilos of wheat, then he divides even without the consent of both. He gives each of the two partners twenty kilos of wheat. All is wheat, it is a single type of goods, and there is no difference in the wheat. And in weight, both are given equally, i.e., twenty kilos each, so no one will suffer any harm. Therefore, even if one is not pleased, the qadi enforces division. But if the goods are of two types, for example ten cloths and forty kilos of wheat, then without the consent of both, he cannot give cloths to one and wheat to the other, because the two types are different. In that case, the consent of both is necessary.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the compulsory division of fungible goods (mithliyyat). The author explains that if the property consists of a single type of good, such as wheat, the qadi can enforce division even against the will of a partner. This is because the goods are identical and can be divided equally by weight or measure without any qualitative difference, thus no harm occurs. However, if the property consists of two different types of goods, such as cloth and wheat, the qadi cannot enforce a division that gives one partner cloth and the other wheat without their mutual consent. This is because the types are distinct and valuation might differ, so harm or inequality could result. The ruling is based on the principle that compulsory partition (qismah jabriyyah) is only allowed when no harm results from the division. جنس (jins): Type or category of goods; e.g., wheat is one jins, cloth is another.
رضامندی (rizamandi): Consent; mutual agreement of the partners to a proposed division.

Key Takeaway

Division with Absent Heir and Indivisible Property
Ruling on division with absent heir and indivisible property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi judge can divide inherited property when an heir is absent, and explain the ruling on dividing property that cannot be physically divided without loss.

Core Idea
A judge may divide property with an absent heir by appointing a proxy; indivisible items require consent or valuation.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Sameri addresses a practical problem in inheritance: what happens when some heirs are present but one is absent? The Hanafi school, relying on the Quranic command to fulfill trusts, allows the judge to proceed with division under strict conditions. A related issue is how to handle items that cannot be divided without destroying their utility, such as a well or a bathhouse. The ruling balances the rights of present heirs with the protection of the absent one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: division of inherited property when an heir is absent. The ruling is that the judge can divide at the request of present heirs subject to conditions, and must appoint a proxy for the absent heir.
The proxy safeguards the absent heir's share.
2
List the conditions for division
Identify each condition stated: (1) at least two heirs appear requesting division, (2) they prove the death of the deceased, (3) they prove the number of heirs, (4) the property is in their possession. These are required for the judge to proceed.
Two requesters serve as witnesses; possession serves as circumstantial evidence.
3
Understand the rationale behind conditions
Analyze why each condition exists: two requesters act as witnesses to death and inheritance; possession is qarinah (indication) that the property is indeed inherited; the proxy fulfills the amanah (trust) toward the absent heir.
The Quranic verse 4:58 is cited as evidence for the duty to fulfill trusts.
4
Examine the ruling on indivisible property
Note that items like a bathhouse, well, or waterwheel cannot be physically divided because they lose utility. The judge should not force division without consent of all co-owners. Instead, the item can be valued and given to one co-owner in exchange for compensation, as supported by the hadith on freeing a share in a slave.
Valuation is a way to avoid loss.
5
Apply the overarching principle
The principle: when circumstantial evidence (qarinah) strongly indicates the truth of the claimants' case, the judge may proceed with division. This ensures justice for both present and absent heirs.
This principle balances evidentiary requirements with practical necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشركاء واذا حضروا رثان عند القاضي واقاما البينة على الوفاة وعدد الورثة والدار فى ايديهم ومعهم وارث غائب قسمها القاضى بطلب الحاضرين وينصب ایسی چیز جو ایک ہی ہو اور تقسیم کرنے کے بعد کسی کے لئے قابل استفادہ نہ رہے جیسے غسل خانہ ، کنواں، پن چکی ، ان چیزوں کو دوٹکڑوں میں تقسیم کر دیں تو استفادے کے قابل نہیں رہتی ہیں۔ اس لئے شرکاء کی رضا مندی کے بغیر تقسیم نہ کرے۔ البتہ ایک شکل ہے کہ اس کی قیمت لگا کر کسی ایک کو دیدے اور اس سے آدھی قیمت وصول کر لے۔ قیمت لگانے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من اعتق شركا له في عبد فكان له مال يبلغ ثمن العبد قوم العبد عليه قيمة عدل فاعطى شركائه حصصهم وعتق عليه العبد ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اعتق عبدا بین اثنین ادامه بین الشرکاء ، ص ۳۲۲، نمبر ۲۵۲۲ / مسلم شریف، باب من اعتق شر کا ءلہ فی عبد ص ۴۹۱ نمبر ۱۵۰۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ غلام کی قیمت لگائی جائے گی اور پھر حصہ داروں کو قیمت دی جائے گی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہاں پوری چیز تقسیم نہیں ہوسکتی ہو وہاں چیز کی قیمت لگا کر حصہ داروں کو دو اور توافق پیدا کر دو۔ اصول جہاں تقسیم کرنے میں دونوں کو نقصان ہو وہاں دونوں کی رضامندی کے بغیر تقسیم نہیں کی جائے گی۔ حمام : غسل خانہ بئر : کنواں، رحی : پن چکی ، جس سے پانی نکالتے ہیں۔ اور دوارث قاضی کے پاس حاضر ہوں اور وفات پر بعینہ قائم کریں اور ورثہ کی تعداد پر اور مکان ان کے قبضے میں ہو اور ان کے ساتھ غائب وارث ہو پھر بھی قاضی حاضرین کی طلب پر تقسیم کر دے۔ اور غائب کے لئے ایک وکیل مقرر کر دے جو اس کے حصے پر قبضہ کرے۔ دو وارث قاضی کے پاس حاضر ہو کر دو بات کرے۔ ایک تو مورث کی وفات پر بینہ قائم کرے کہ واقعی وہ مر چکا ہے۔ دوسری بات یہ کرے کہ ورثہ کی کل تعداد کتنی ہے اس پر گواہی قائم کرے۔ اور تیسری بات یہ ہے کہ گھر مطالبہ کرنے والوں کے قبضے میں ہو۔ اس صورت میں وارث غائب ہو پھر بھی قاضی گھر تقسیم کر دے گا اور جو وارث غائب ہو اس کے لئے وکیل مقرر کرے تا کہ وہ غائب کے حصے پر قبضہ کر کے اس کی حفاظت کرے اور جب غائب آجائے تو اس کے حوالے کر دے۔ ان چارشقوں کی وجوہات یہ ہیں (۱) تقسیم کا مطالبہ کرنے والے دو آدمی اس لئے ہوں کہ وہ دو گواہ کے درجے میں ہو جائیں گے اور یقین کیا جا سکے گا کہ واقعی مورث مر چکا ہے۔ اور ورثہ کی تعداد اتنی ہی ہے۔ اور اگر مطالبہ کرنے والا ایک آدمی ہو تو یقین نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے کہ مورث کی موت ہو چکی ہے۔ اور ورثہ کی تعداد اتنی ہی ہے۔ کیونکہ شہادت کی تعداد ایک نہیں ہوتی دو ہوتی ہے (۲) ایک نکتہ یہ بھی ہے کہ ایک مدعی اور دوسرا مدعی علیہ کے درجے میں ہوگا ۔ میت جو غائب ہے اس غائب کے خلاف فیصلہ نہیں ہوگا، کیونکہ غائب پر فیصلہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کوئی مشترکہ غلام آزاد کرے اور اس کے پاس اتنا مال ہو کہ غلام کی قیمت ہو جائے تو اس پر غلام کی عادل قیمت لگائی جائے گی۔ اور اس کے شریکوں کو ان کے حصے دیئے جائیں گے۔ اور پورا غلام آزاد کرنے والے پر آزاد ہوگا۔ دوسرا آدمی مدعی علیه حاضر کے درجے میں ہو جائے گا۔ گھر مطالبہ کرنے والوں کے قبضہ میں ہو تب تقسیم کیا جائے گا۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قبضہ ہونا اس بات کا یقین دلاتا ہے کہ مورث مرا ہے اور یہ لوگ واقعی اس گھر کے وارث ہیں۔ کیونکہ غائب وارث کا قبضہ ہو تو شبہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ کسی اور کا گھر ہے جس کے بارے میں قاضی صاحب کو چکما دے کر اپنے لئے تقسیم کروانا چاہتے ہیں ۔ لیکن چونکہ گھر مطالبہ کرنے والے کے ہاتھ میں ہے اس لئے قرینہ یہی ہے کہ گھر ان ہی کے مورث کا ہے۔ غائب کے لئے وکیل متعین کرے۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ غائب کی امانت ہے اس لئے اس کی حفاظت کرنا اور اس تک پہنچانا قاضی کا کام ہے۔ آیت میں موجود ہے۔ ان الله يأمركم أن تؤدوا الامانات الى اهلها واذا حكمتم بين الناس ان تحكموا بالعدل ان الله نعما يعظكم به (آیت ۵۸، سورۃ النساء ۴ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ امانت والوں کو امانت پہنچاؤ۔ اور یہ بھی ہے کہ صحیح فیصلہ کیا کرو۔ اور یہ امانت اسی صورت میں پہنچے گی کہ غائب کے لئے وکیل متعین کیا جائے۔ اس طرح فیصلہ کرنے اور تقسیم کرنے میں حاضرین کا فائدہ ہے کہ ان کو جلدی حق مل گیا اور غائب کا بھی فائدہ ہے کہ وکیل کے ذریعہ اس کا حق محفوظ ہو گیا۔ اصول یہ تین مسئلے اس اصول پر متفرع ہیں کہ قرینے سے معلوم ہو جائے کہ یہ لوگ سچ بول رہے ہیں اور حق مطالبہ ہے تو مال تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ وينصب للغائب وكيلا يقبض نصيبه
Partners: If heirs appear before the judge and establish evidence of death, number of heirs, and that the house is in their possession, and there is an absent heir, the judge divides it at the request of the present ones and appoints... (explanation of indivisible items)... The evidence for valuation is this hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: Whoever frees his share in a slave and has wealth sufficient to reach the value of the slave, the slave is valued with a just value, he gives his partners their shares, and the slave is freed. ... (commentary) ... And he appoints for the absent one a proxy to take possession of his share.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage from the commentary of Al-Sameri explains the ruling on dividing inherited property when some heirs are present and one is absent. The matn states that if two (or more) heirs present themselves to the judge, establish the death of the deceased, the number of heirs, and that the property is in their possession, then even if there is an absent heir, the judge may divide the property at the request of the present ones. The judge must appoint a proxy (wakil) for the absent heir to take possession of his share. The commentary first addresses a preliminary issue: items that cannot be physically divided without losing utility (like a bathhouse, well, or waterwheel). The judge should not force division of such items without consent of all partners. Instead, he can have the item valued and give it to one partner in exchange for half the value, using the hadith on freeing a share in a slave as evidence. That hadith establishes the principle of valuation in joint property. The commentary then details the conditions for dividing with an absent heir: the request must come from at least two heirs (equivalent to two witnesses), they must prove the death and the number of heirs, and the property must be in their possession. The reasons for these conditions are explained: two requesters serve as witnesses to the death; the presence of the property in their hands is a strong indicator of their inheritance rights; and the absent heir cannot be judged against without a proxy. The judge's appointment of a proxy is based on the Quranic command to fulfill trusts (Surah Nisa 4:58). This ensures the absent heir's share is preserved. The section concludes with the overarching principle: when circumstantial evidence (qarinah) indicates the truth of the claimants and their right to demand division, the property is divided; otherwise not.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners, either voluntarily or by court order.
وكيل (wakil): Proxy appointed by judge to take possession and safeguard the share of the absent heir.
قرينة (qarinah): Circumstantial evidence that indicates the truth of the claim, such as possession of the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must at least two heirs request division from the judge in the case of an absent heir?
A) To match the number of witnesses required for testimony
B) To ensure the absent heir's rights are not violated
C) Because the judge cannot act alone
D) To prove the property is inherited

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi judge can divide inherited property with an absent heir under strict conditions, relying on the Quranic duty to fulfill trusts and appointing a proxy to protect the absent heir.

No Division for Co-Purchasers When One Absent
Exception: no division for co-purchasers when one absent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi exception that a judge does not divide jointly purchased property in the absence of a co-purchaser, and explain the three reasons for this distinction from inheritance.

Core Idea
A judge defers division of purchased property until all purchasers are present, unlike inherited property which is divided urgently.

This lesson examines a key exception in Hanafi law of division (qisma). While inherited property is divided quickly to prevent loss, jointly purchased property requires all owners to be present or consent before the judge proceeds. The commentary provides three distinct reasons for this rule, rooted in the nature of ownership and procedural justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of co-ownership
Recognize that the passage distinguishes between inherited property (waratha) and purchased property (mushtariyayn). Each has different rules for judicial division.
Inheritance is from a deceased person; purchase involves living owners.
2
State the rule for purchased property
The judge does not divide the property if one co-purchaser is absent. This is the exception that contrasts with the general rule for inheritance.
The rule applies even if two out of three purchasers are present and request division.
3
Extract the three reasons from the commentary
Read the commentary carefully: (1) no urgency because purchasers guard their own property; (2) risk of fraud since the absent may have a larger share; (3) procedural: judgment against an absent person (qada 'ala al-gha'ib) is not allowed in purchase context.
The third reason references the broader Hanafi principle against judging absent persons.
4
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Use the three reasons to determine the outcome in a hypothetical case, such as two people buying a shop and one being abroad.
Confirm that the absence of any one purchaser blocks division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانوا مشتريين لم يقسم مع غيبة احدهم مثلا تین آدمیوں نے مل کر ایک گھر خریدا۔ پھر دو آدمی ملکر قاضی کے پاس آئے کہ مجھے تقسیم کر کے دیں۔ اور ایک خریدار غائب ہے تو قاضی گھر تقسیم نہ کرے۔ وراثت کی شکل میں مال میت کا تھا جب تک تقسیم کر کے نہ دیں، وارثین اس کی حفاظت میں لا پرواہی کریں گے اس لئے اس کو جلدی تقسیم کرکے دینا ضروری ہے۔ اور خریدے ہوئے مال کی ضیاع کا خریدار کو فکر ہے اس لئے اس کو جلدی تقسیم کرنا ضروری نہیں جب تک کہ غائب نہ آجائے (۲) غائب کا اپنا لگایا ہوا مال ہے۔ اس لئے یہ ممکن ہے کہ اس سے زیادہ حصہ لگایا ہو اور حاضرین چکما دے کر زیادہ لے لینا چاہتا ہو اس لئے غائب کی حاضری کے بعد پتا چلے گا کہ اس کا حصہ کتنا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی حاضری کے بغیر تقسیم نہ کرے (۳) یہ نکتہ بھی ہے کہ مورث دنیا سے جا چکا ہے اس لئے وارث اس کی جانب سے خصم ہوں گے اس لئے قضا علی الغائب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور خریدنے کی شکل میں غائب آدمی دنیا حاشیہ : ( الف ) اللہ تعالی تم کو حکم دیتے ہیں کہ امانت والے کو امانت پہنچاؤ، اور جب تم لوگوں کے درمیان فیصلہ کرو تو انصاف کے ساتھ فیصلہ کرو۔ اللہ تعالی تمہیں اچھی نصیحت کرتے ہیں۔
And if they are purchasers, it is not divided in the absence of one of them. For example, three people bought a house together. Then two come to the judge saying 'divide for us', and one purchaser is absent, then the judge does not divide the house. In the case of inheritance, the property belonged to the deceased; until division, the heirs would be negligent in its preservation, so early division is necessary. But for purchased property, the purchasers are concerned about loss, so early division is not necessary until the absent one comes. (2) The absent one's own money is invested; it is possible he contributed a larger share and the present ones fraudulently want to take more, so only after his presence will his share be known. (3) The deceased has left this world, so the heirs represent him; thus judgment against the absent is not valid. In purchase, the absent person is alive. Footnote: (a) 'Indeed Allah commands you to deliver trusts to their owners...'
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents an exception to the previous ruling: if the co-owners are purchasers (i.e., they jointly bought the property), the judge does not divide it in the absence of one of them. The commentary explains three reasons for this distinction. First, urgency: in inheritance, the property was owned by the deceased and the heirs may neglect it, so quick division is necessary to avoid loss. In purchase, the co-owners are already concerned about their property, so there is no urgency. Second, risk of fraud: the absent purchaser may have contributed a larger share, and the present ones might mistakenly or fraudulently claim a larger portion; only when the absent one is present can the exact shares be determined. Third, procedural difference: in inheritance, the deceased is gone, so the heirs are his representatives; judgment against the absent heir is not permissible because you cannot judge against a deceased person's representative? Actually, the text says 'qada' ala al-gha'ib' is not valid, meaning you cannot give judgment against an absent person. But in purchase, the absent person is alive and can be present, so judgment should await his presence. The footnote repeats the Quranic verse about trusts and justice, emphasizing that delivering the trust (the absent person's share) requires proper procedure.

Key Terms
مشتريين (mushtariyayn): Co-purchasers who bought the property together, as opposed to heirs.
قضا علی الغائب (qada 'ala al-gha'ib): Judgment against an absent person, which is not permissible in Hanafi law except in certain cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the judge not divide purchased property when one co-purchaser is absent?
A) Because the absent person may have paid a larger share
B) Because the property is not inherited
C) Because there is no urgency and risk of fraud
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the judge does not divide jointly purchased property in the absence of a co-purchaser, unlike inherited property, to prevent loss and fraud.

The Method of Partitioning Property with Lots
Describes the procedure for dividing property and drawing lots

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for partitioning jointly owned property and explain the evidentiary basis for using lots.

Core Idea
Partition with lots ensures fairness and is a sunnah method based on the Prophet's division of Khaybar.

This passage describes the recommended method for a judge to divide property among co-owners. The procedure includes measuring, equalizing, valuing buildings, and separating each share with its rights of way and water channels. Then the judge draws lots. This is supported by the Prophet's practice at Khaybar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the procedural steps
List the five preparatory actions mentioned: measurement, equalization, pacing, valuation of buildings, and physical separation of each share with its pathway and water channel.
These ensure each share is independent and free from encumbrances.
2
Understand the purpose of lots
Why does the judge write names and draw lots? To ensure fairness and avoid accusations of favoritism among co-owners.
Lots are a tool for impartial assignment when shares are equal after adjustment.
3
Trace the dalil
The hadith of Bashir bin Yasar: the Prophet divided Khaybar into 36 shares, each comprising 100 portions. This act demonstrates the permissibility and method of partition with lots.
The hadith is a Sunnah ahad with zanni thubut but qati dalala.
4
Classify the ruling
The procedure is classified as sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended), not wajib, because it is based on the Prophet's action (fi'l) which indicates istihbab.
The Hanafi school holds that the judge's following this method is meritorious but not obligatory.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
Imagine a jointly owned plot of land. How would a Hanafi judge implement this procedure step by step? Consider measurement, adjustment for unequal contributions, valuation of structures, and allocation of access rights.
The procedure can be adapted to modern property division while maintaining its essential fairness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يقسمه ويعدله ويذرعه ويقوم البناء ويفرز كل نصيب عن الباقي بطريقه وشربه حتى لا يكون لنصيب بعضهم بنصيب الآخر تعلق ثم يكتب اساميهم و يجعلها قرعة عن بشير بن يسار مولى الانصار عن رجال من اصحاب النبي ان رسول الله لما ظهر على خيبر قسمها على ستة وثلاثين سهما جمع كل سهم مائة سهم
He measures, equalizes, paces, values the building, and separates each share from the remainder with its pathway and water channel so that no share has a connection to another's share. Then he writes their names and makes them a lottery. From Bashir bin Yasar, the freed slave of the Ansar, from men among the Companions of the Prophet, that when the Messenger of Allah conquered Khaybar, he divided it into thirty-six shares, each share comprising one hundred portions.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage states the recommended procedure for a judge when partitioning property among co-owners. It begins by describing the preparatory steps: measurement, equalization, pacing to determine dimensions, valuation of buildings, and physical separation of each share along with its right of way (tariq) and water channel (sharb) to ensure each share is independent. Then the judge writes the names of the co-owners and prepares slips for a lottery. The passage also provides a Prophetic precedent: the division of Khaybar land into 36 shares, each of 100 portions. This demonstrates the legitimacy of using lots in partition. The Hanafi school holds that this method is sunnah for the judge to ensure justice and avoid accusations of favoritism.

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Partition of jointly owned property into distinct shares.
قرعة (qur'a): Lots or a lottery used to assign shares to co-owners.
شرب (sharb): Water channel or right to water passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of drawing lots (qur'a) in property partition according to the commentary?
A) To make the division legally binding.
B) To ensure fairness and avoid accusations of favoritism.
C) To determine the value of each share.
D) To exclude certain heirs from the division.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi partition procedure, including lots, is a sunnah method ensuring fairness, grounded in the Prophet's division of Khaybar.

Inclusion of Dirhams and Dinars in Partition Requires Consent
Ruling that gold and silver money are not included in partition without mutual consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on including currency in property partition and explain the dalil from the two hadiths.

Core Idea
Including money in a partition becomes a sale that requires mutual consent.

This lesson examines a crucial principle in Islamic property law: the distinction between pure division and exchange. The Hanafi school rules that currency (dirhams and dinars) cannot be automatically included in a partition of real estate because it constitutes a sale transaction. The passage presents two hadiths to support this ruling. By the end, you will understand why consent is necessary and how the proofs apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is including dirhams/dinars in a property partition without mutual consent. The ruling is that it is prohibited (haram) and invalid.
The prohibition is specific to currency; other movables may be included with consent.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadiths: (1) The hadith of Imran bin Husain about a man who freed six slaves at death; the Prophet divided them by lot freeing two and keeping four. (2) The hadith of al-Nu'man bin Bashir about the ship analogy.
Both hadiths are from the Sunnah and have a zanni level of transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith shows division by lot for multiple movable items (slaves) is permissible. The second uses analogy: those on a ship who draw lots for compartments must accept exchange because it is necessary; but in partition, including currency is not necessary, so consent is required.
The key distinction: partition is about dividing existing shares, not creating exchange unless unavoidable.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools allow inclusion of insignificant amounts of currency without consent, viewing it as a minor adjustment.
The Hanafi school rejects this because any inclusion changes the legal nature of the transaction.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that currency cannot be included without consent. This is based on the principle that exchange of ribawi items requires equality and mutual consent.
The tarjih is from the Zahir al-Riwayah texts; there is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf reported.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يُدخل في القسمة الدراهم والدنانير الا بتراضيهم فان قسم. عن عمران بن حصين ان رجلا كان له ستة مملوكين ليس له مال غيرهم فاعتقهم عند موته فجزأهم رسول الله فاعتق اثنين وارق اربعة. سمعت النعمان بن بشير عن النبي قال مثل القائم على حدود الله والواقع فيها كمثل قوم استهموا على سفينة فاصاب بعضهم اعلاها وبعضهم اسفلها
And dirhams and dinars are not included in the partition except with their mutual consent. If he divides... From Imran bin Husain that a man had six slaves and no other wealth, so he freed them at his death. The Messenger of Allah then divided them: he freed two and kept four as slaves. I heard al-Nu'man bin Bashir from the Prophet saying: The example of the one who upholds the limits of Allah and the one who falls into them is like people who drew lots on a ship; some got the upper part and some the lower part.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage addresses a key principle in Islamic partition law: different categories of property (real estate and currency) cannot be commingled in a single partition without the explicit consent of all co-owners. The reason is that including dirhams and dinars in the division of a house, for example, constitutes a sale or exchange (bai') since the money is used to equalize shares that are unequal in value. Such a transaction requires mutual agreement. The passage provides two hadith proofs: the first from Imran bin Husain shows that the Prophet divided slaves (movable property) by lot; the second from al-Nu'man bin Bashir uses the analogy of a ship to justify the permissibility of exchange when necessary, such as when a share includes a water channel that falls into another's property.

Key Terms
دراهم ودنانير (darahim wa dananir): Silver and gold coins, used as currency.
تراض (taradi): Mutual consent of all parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are dirhams and dinars not included in a property partition without mutual consent according to the commentary?
A) Because they are prohibited (haram) to include.
B) Because including them constitutes a sale, which requires consent.
C) Because they are not divisible.
D) Because the judge does not have authority over them.

Key Takeaway
Dirhams and dinars (currency) cannot be included in a property partition without the mutual consent of all co-owners because it constitutes a sale.
